# **741 – Inventing Her Own Recovery Art, Halving the Time Needed**

In that instant, a powerful surge burst from Alicia’s body, making the cavern tremble ever so slightly.

Lili looked toward Yae-hime with a hint of concern, only to realize that the latter was completely unaffected. Looking back at Alicia, she also appeared perfectly calm.

‘They’re fine… thank goodness.’ She pressed a hand to her chest and let out a quiet breath.

As the saying went, once bitten by a snake, one feared even a coiled rope for years. Even now, she still felt lingering dread, worried that something might go wrong. Fortunately, her Little Hime was as steady as ever.

Alicia looked tranquil on the surface, yet inside her emotions surged like a churning sea. ‘Amazing. Such intricate control over energies… this is the first time I have ever felt something like this!’

At this moment, two distinct energies were circulating rapidly within her body. One glimmered green-blue. The other glowed earthy yellow. They were earth energy and Yae-hime’s wood energy. The two powers formed dual vortices, swirling repeatedly before twisting together like a two-colored braid. Finally, they blended into one, becoming a large orb of interwoven green and yellow light.

‘This is truly miraculous!’ Alicia viewed her body from within and couldn’t help but marvel. But the next scene shook her even more. That spinning sphere of dual color suddenly released countless threads, which swiftly and cleanly merged into her limbs and bones. They felt like spring rain falling on fertile soil, soothing and refreshing.

‘Amazing… feels so good… this feeling is completely different from my own method. This nourishes gently and silently, whereas mine is more like rough devouring!’ The former caused no harm at all, while the latter damaged the body and wasted energy.

Alicia clearly sensed that Yae-hime was weaving every strand of power seamlessly into her entire body. Exquisite was the only word for it.

Just then, Yae-hime’s hands began to glide across her body. The earth energy and wood energy seeped through her from outside to inside and inside to outside, nourishing Alicia bit by bit. It felt so good it made her very soul tremble.

If Yae-hime hadn’t instructed her earlier to remember the flow of the energies, Alicia would have already ascended straight into bliss. Suppressing the urge to soar, she focused intently on memorizing everything.

Gradually, she began to sense a kind of profound, indescribable mystery. As time passed, most of the earth energy inside the cave had already been depleted.

“You can try imitating my previous method now.” Suddenly, Yae-hime spoke.

“Yes.” Alicia nodded lightly, then immediately began her attempt.

Yae-hime withdrew her hands, exhaling a long, murky breath. Her face was filled with exhaustion. With her current strength, manipulating the forces inside Alicia’s body was still somewhat strenuous.

After all, Alicia was a Legend-ranked figure; her physique had long surpassed the human realm by several layers, making the difficulty far higher than Yae-hime initially expected. Still, despite the hardship, the benefits were immense.

Understanding the internal structure of a legend-rank body like this would greatly aid her future breakthroughs. The difficulty would decrease by a considerable margin.

‘A pity that I still cannot grasp the deeper mysteries of the legend rank.’ Human desire was never easily satisfied, and Yae-hime was no exception.

She gave a wry smile, then looked toward Alicia. The girl’s brows were lightly furrowed, her complexion pale, as if she had encountered a problem. Yae-hime made no move to help. It wasn’t because she was unwilling, but because she believed Alicia’s talent was more than enough to overcome such difficulties.

And sure enough, in less than ten seconds, her expression softened and even curved into a faint smile.

‘No wonder she’s the one-in-a-million genius of the Jade Empire.’ Through her perception, Yae-hime could see Alicia repeating her earlier technique. Although still clumsy and rough, with more time and practice she would surely grow proficient.

‘With this method, her recovery time will definitely shorten. All that matters is whether Alicia can fully master it.’ This recovery method was something Yae-hime created after fully understanding Alicia’s body. It was a complete original.

Even she herself could not use it. Their physical traits were simply too different. But even if she could use it, she would not. Because this method was derived from the Green Emperor’s Longevity Manual, and the two simply did not belong to the same level at all.

After watching for a moment and confirming that everything was normal, Yae-hime stepped down from the bed. At once, Lili stood up quickly and yielded the only chair in the room.

The moment Yae-hime sat down, a small figure immediately plopped onto her lap. The little head, tied with golden twin tails, leaned firmly against her.

“Reserved,” she whispered.

Hearing that, Yae-hime couldn’t help rolling her eyes. So she really was treating her like a living chair?

“Was everything solved perfectly?” Lili asked softly.

“Mm. If nothing unexpected happens, in a few days Alicia should be able to recover—no, she should finish absorbing the inheritance power inside the Inheritance Jewel. Her strength should improve quite a bit compared to before.” Yae-hime lowered her voice as she spoke.

“That’s wonderful.” Lili clenched her small hands, relief warming her expression. Only at this moment did she truly relax. Immediately after, a wave of drowsiness washed over her. Drawn in by the dream demon’s subtle influence, she slowly closed her eyes. Her consciousness sank deeper and deeper until she finally drifted into sleep.

Hearing that steady, gentle breathing, Yae-hime paused in surprise before realizing that Lili had fallen asleep.

‘She must be exhausted.’ Thinking about how she had been running around nonstop for Alicia since last night, with both her mind and body stretched to the limit, Yae-hime felt a twinge of heartache.

And, just a little, she felt touched.

‘So this is what having family feels like… it’s nice.’ As an orphan, the thing she had always longed for most was a home. A home with family. ‘Once things settle down here, I should return to Goose City to visit my parents’ graves.’

Though her memories of them had grown almost completely blurred, the proper filial duty was something she still intended to fulfill.

‘I should also visit the orphanage. I didn’t manage to reach them on the phone last time, and I’m still a little worried.’ For now, she still couldn’t return to her male form, making it hard to call them again. Besides, she simply couldn’t step away at the moment.

“Zzz Zzz Zzz…” Listening to the peaceful breathing against her chest, Yae-hime let out a quiet laugh. She then held Lili gently to keep her from slipping over.

On the other side, Alicia was progressing smoothly, greedily absorbing both earth energy and wood energy as they nourished her body. Feeling bored, Yae-hime held Lili with one arm and opened the game interface with the other, browsing the forum.

But as soon as she entered, she saw a flood of posts filled with sour players criticizing her. After reading through a few threads, she finally understood the whole situation. “I didn’t cheat,” she whispered.

‘The system did.’ She added that silently in her heart. Of course, that was just her own little joke. ‘Being reborn is my own ability too, what’s there to be jealous about?’

She couldn’t be bothered with these sour grapes and their so-called accusations. Continuing to scroll, she found the rest of the posts equally sour, the acidity almost stinging her nose.

She closed the forum with a flick of her hand. Yae-hime suddenly remembered Little Fairy and Yunuen. ‘I wonder if those two have been leveling properly.’

…

At that moment, several hours’ travel away from Jade City, deep within a swamp, Yunuen and Little Fairy were locked in a fierce battle.

+++

# **742 – Now Then… How Should This Money Be Spent?**

“Heyah!” Yunuen charged straight into the cluster of monsters. Her staff swept out as she spun, and a blood-red whirlwind surged forth. The swamp toads were instantly lifted into the air, flung about like rag dolls.

In the next moment, Little Fairy, who had long finished readying her bow, pulled the string skyward. Her Multi-Shot burst outward in a full barrage. The two coordinated seamlessly, slaughtering the nearby beasts with wild momentum. In less than ten minutes, the entire area had been completely cleared.

“Let’s rest for a moment.” Yunuen’s face had turned a little pale.

“Mm, I’m tired too.” Little Fairy seemed to be in about the same condition.

The two left the swamp and moved to a relatively safer spot to rest.

“Getting to level thirty takes so much experience.” Little Fairy stared at her experience bar in helpless awe.

“Yeah, it’s way too hard. If Princess had time to carry us, it’d go so much faster.” Yunuen leaned back against a tree trunk, gazing at the distant scenery as she spoke calmly.

“Too bad Princess is so busy,” Little Fairy said.

“Mm. It’s been a while since we last saw her in the game.”

Ever since leaving Jade City, the two of them had not regrouped with Yae-hime and had simply been leveling in the surrounding areas.

“Speaking of which, Yunuen, how are you planning to spend all that money you won?” Little Fairy asked. The money she referred to was the bet they had placed before Yae-hime’s duel with Lucky.

Yunuen and Little Fairy had staked everything they had. The former bet fifty thousand, while the latter bet ten thousand. At the time, Yae-hime’s odds were seven-to-one. Which meant Yunuen had received three hundred fifty thousand in winnings, netting a pure profit of three hundred thousand. Little Fairy received seventy thousand, earning sixty thousand in pure profit. For them, that was already a fortune.

“I plan to give half to my family and keep the other half for myself,” Yunuen said.

“To save up for an apartment?” Having spent quite some time together now, Little Fairy already understood Yunuen very well, including her family situation.

“An apartment? No need. The money I earn from apothecary is being managed by Princess. At this rate, it probably won’t be long before I have a new home!” Yunuen spoke cheerfully.

Right now, she and her parents were staying at the Rosen Hotel. It was comfortable, but still not truly their own home. As the saying went, even a golden or silver nest couldn’t compare to one’s own humble den.

“That’s nice… I want my own house too.” Little Fairy spoke with a trace of envy. Ever since her father passed away, she had been living with her uncle’s family. Being dependent on others never felt very good.

Of course, she was still grateful to the uncle’s family who had taken her in. After all, taking care of a disabled child with crippled legs was already adding a heavy burden to their household.

At that moment, Yunuen gave Little Fairy a slow, assessing look, making her feel uneasy all over.

“W-What is it? Do I have something weird on me?”

“I was just thinking… the equipment you’re wearing is probably worth tens of millions,” Yunuen said.

Little Fairy blinked in surprise, then realized that her Epic gear and Rare gear really were worth several tens of millions. “Suddenly turning into a rich lady… it doesn’t feel real at all.” She let out a wry smile.

“I don’t feel real either. Ever since we latched onto Princess’ thigh, it’s like the whole world changed.” Yunuen lifted her head, shading her eyes from the sunlight filtering through the leaves as she spoke softly.

“Yeah… it really changed.” Little Fairy lowered her head. Thinking back on everything that had happened over the past few days, it all felt like a dream. A beautiful dream, almost unreal.

“Right, how are you planning to spend your winnings?” Yunuen suddenly asked.

“I…” Although she was the one who brought up the topic, Little Fairy truly hadn’t decided how to use the money.

Seventy thousand. With her salary at the flower shop, she would need to save for two full years without eating or drinking to reach that amount.

In truth, among young people these days, very few had seventy thousand in savings. Receiving such a sum all of a sudden… she really didn’t know how to spend it.[1](#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119695)　

“Not buying new clothes or cosmetics?” Yunuen blinked her big eyes as she asked.

Little Fairy shook her head. “I don’t need those for now.” As soon as she said that, one person suddenly came to mind.

‘I wonder if he’s managed to get through his troubles… Too bad I don’t have his number.’ Right then, Little Fairy finally realized how she wanted to use the money.[2](#easy-footnote-bottom-2-119695) She wanted to help Yaeger through his difficulties.

Even now, she still cared about the boy who had once helped her. Unfortunately, she had no way of contacting him at all.

If it had been anyone else borrowing money without leaving any contact information, Little Fairy would have absolutely assumed they were a scammer. ‘The situation that day had been a little special. It was only natural he hadn’t thought about leaving his contact details.’

Remembering Yaeger’s condition at the time, Little Fairy still felt a pang of pain in her chest. ‘I hope he’s safe… I really do.’ She made a silent wish in her heart.

“Little Fairy, what are you thinking about?” At that moment, Yunuen waved a hand in front of her face.

“Ah? I—I wasn’t thinking about anything!” Little Fairy snapped back to reality and answered in fluster.

“Heheh, you’re that panicked and still claiming you’re not thinking about anything? Come on, tell me!” Yunuen leaned closer with a comically exaggerated face.

“N-Nothing at all! Break time’s over, let’s keep leveling!” When it came to matters involving Yaeger, Little Fairy had no intention of telling anyone just yet. Not even someone as close as Yunuen.

“Heheh, the more you don’t want to say it, the more I want to know.” Yunuen took full advantage of the opportunity, her hands almost wrapping around Little Fairy.

Little Fairy reacted with startling speed, slipping away like a startled rabbit.

“Tell meee!” Naturally, Yunuen wasn’t going to let her go and immediately chased after her. Under the sunlight, the breath of youth scattered freely into the air.

---

Time flew by, and before they knew it, evening had arrived.

Lili slowly opened her eyes, her consciousness still a little hazy.

“So comfortable…” She felt the warmth and softness behind her and stretched like a cat.

“You’re awake.” Suddenly, a voice came from above. Hearing that familiar tone, Lili’s thoughts kicked into motion, and her mind gradually cleared.

“Ah… I fell asleep…” she murmured with a faint flush across her pretty face.

“Mm, you slept very soundly.” Yae-hime chuckled.

“Uu…” Lili lowered her head, letting out a soft, embarrassed sound that made her look incredibly adorable.

“Your sleeping face is really cute,” Yae-hime teased.

“You’re awful.” Lili gave Yae-hime’s thigh a light pinch and spoke in a coquettish tone.

Then she lifted her head and looked over at Alicia. By now, the earth energy and wood energy around the girl had completely disappeared. “Is it over?” she asked softly.

“More or less.” Yae-hime’s pupils instantly turned a vivid jade-green as she used them to see through Alicia’s condition.

The two waited for about three minutes before Alicia finally opened her eyes, an irrepressible excitement spreading over her face. ‘What I gained in just one afternoon was actually more than what I managed in the past few days!’

At this pace, she would be back at her peak in just four or five days!

“Sis, how do you feel?” Seeing that expression, Lili couldn’t help asking.

“I’ve never felt this good before!” Alicia looked over at them, her voice filled with excitement.

“Then just keep recovering at this pace. Whatever you do, don’t get impatient and push too hard,” Yae-hime reminded her.

Hearing that, Alicia immediately felt a little embarrassed, a faint blush rising to her cheeks.

“It’s getting late. There are still things waiting for me back in Aoma Village, so I won’t stay much longer.” Yae-hime gently patted Lili’s head, then went on, “If anything comes up, just send someone to Aoma Village to find me. I’ll basically be staying there these next few days. Also, Lili… are you free?”

# **Footnotes:**

1. Syl: I’m not even young anymore and I still don’t have 70k in savings… what did I do wrong in life?

2. Syl: Even now, she’s thinking of helping male Yaeger, what an absolute keeper!

# **743 – The Onset of a New Storm**

“Me?” Suddenly questioned, Lili looked a little puzzled.

“Yes. I have something I want your help with. Are you free?” Yae-hime asked again.

Lili lifted her gaze at her, then looked toward Alicia.

The latter nodded. “Moon and Nectar are here. It’s fine.”

“Alright.” Lili withdrew her gaze and took Yae-hime’s hand. “Do I need to return to Aoma Village with you?”

“Yes,” Yae-hime replied.

More accurately, not going back to Aoma Village wasn’t an option at all. Considering those Apostles might strike tonight or early tomorrow morning, she naturally hoped Lili would come with her immediately.

‘The Fifth Apostle was already that troublesome. If the Fourth and Third Apostles show up too, I’m done for!’ In reality, her worry was unnecessary. The group of Apostles had already left the Jade Empire and gone off to wreak havoc on the Sky Empire instead.

All that remained for her to deal with was a mess, though not the worst kind of mess.

“Sis, I’ll come right back after I finish things over there.” After speaking to Alicia, Lili turned to Yae-hime again.

“It’s getting dark. Let’s depart.” The danger level of this mountain range differed greatly between day and night. Nighttime was far more perilous. She herself had no issue traveling alone, but bringing Yae-hime with her made things significantly harder.

After all, protecting someone and charging ahead alone were entirely different matters.

Neither of them dragged things out. Once they decided to go, they left immediately. Before long, the cave was left with only Alicia.

“Little Hime grows at a speed that’s downright astonishing… so this is what it means to be a Child of Destiny.” A faint smile appeared on her lips as she whispered to herself. Her expression then gradually turned serious. “Four or five more days, and I can take back what belongs to me. Brother… no, Richard—just you wait!”

From the moment he attacked the underground maze and tried to kill her, Alicia had severed all ties with Richard completely. The two of them were already locked into a life-and-death grudge.

At the same time, in Jade City…

An extravagantly luxurious beast-drawn carriage slowly rolled out from the royal palace. Inside the carriage, Bishop Gurant, draped in a white robe threaded with gold, leaned back against the soft seat, his face openly filled with unrestrained joy.

Although he had long known this outcome was possible, the moment it truly happened brought him a dreamlike sense of fulfillment. It felt as though his entire being had been filled with delight.

“Praise the Goddess!” he suddenly raised both hands high and shouted. Yet not a trace of devotion could be seen in that expression. In this age where the gods no longer walked the world, many things had already decayed.

“This world no longer needs the old ‘gods’… We are the gods of a new era,” Gurant said with a smile as he lowered his hands. A faintly deranged fervor flickered in his expression.

Meanwhile, inside the Church of Light, the High Priest was apologizing profusely to Passat. His groveling posture was no different from that of a lowly servant, and he practically radiated eagerness to serve Passat at every turn.

In response, Passat only curled his lips into a cold, dismissive smile. Someone like this might be good for flattery, but absolutely unreliable for anything else.

‘A girl with a true heart like Irene is the only kind worthy of staying by my side!’ The elegance of that single hammer strike had left a deep mark on Passat’s heart. “I’m absolutely going to make her mine!” He brushed aside a strand of golden hair and declared with sudden confidence.

At those words, the High Priest’s eyelids and mouth twitched at the same time, his heart filled with bitterness. ‘It was me. I clearly made the first move, I approached Passat first, I spoke with him first… so why did that little vixen swoop in ahead of me!?’

He dreamed day and night of forming ties with the prestigious Aslan family. Yet this Passat had inexplicably become infatuated with the vicious, violent fox who had assaulted him. And treated the High Priest’s loyal hints with nothing but cold laughter! It was utterly incomprehensible!

Elsewhere, Irene lay on her bed, letting out a soft sigh, her small face filled with worry. She now knew exactly where the man she hammered came from, and she recalled the Aslan family’s influence across the southern continent. “If I lose the Saintess position over this, I’ll just have to find another solution.”

As for whether she regretted sending Passat flying with that hammer, of course she didn’t regret it one bit. What was done was done. Regret would change nothing. She only feared that losing the position of Saintess might deal a fatal blow to what she needed to accomplish. Other than that, she could not be bothered.

“What should I do…” At that moment, Irene felt an intense headache coming on. Without the Saintess position, she could not enter the Holy Land. That place was one ordinary people could never enter. That place held the very thing she had long dreamed of obtaining. Unfortunately, it now felt farther and farther away from her reach.

“Ugh, I don’t want to think about it anymore!” Irene yanked the blanket over her head, agitation filling her heart. At that moment, a person suddenly came to mind. “If that bad girl were here, it’d be great…”

The “bad girl” she spoke of was undoubtedly referring to Yae-hime. That scourge of the empire feared nothing, had endless wicked ideas, and if she were here, she would definitely come up with a solution!

‘Bad girl, hurry and come help me!’ Irene had never before longed for someone’s help this much. Unfortunately, no matter how loudly she cried out in her heart, the far-away Yae-hime could not hear her.

---

“It’s just gotten dark.” At this moment, Yae-hime and Lili appeared outside the Phantabeast Range. Yae-hime sounded relieved.

Lili nodded lightly. “We didn’t run into anything troublesome, so we saved a lot of time.”

On the way out, they had only encountered a few low-level beasts with no sense of self-preservation. Lili had sliced through them as easily as chopping vegetables, so they never became an issue.

“It’s deserted out here. We can’t even find a beast-drawn carriage. Why don’t we wait here for one to pass?” Yae-hime suggested. She absolutely did not want to run all the way back to Aoma Village, she would break her legs doing that.

Lili considered it briefly. “Yes, let’s wait for a carriage.” The distance to Aoma Village was still quite far. Even if she ran at full speed, it would take time. And while she could make it there quickly, Yae-hime definitely could not.

The difference in their abilities was still very obvious. So after a brief moment of thought, Lili accepted her Little Hime’s suggestion. The two of them waited by the roadside for less than five minutes before a luxurious beast-drawn carriage approached.

“This one will do.” Yae-hime said as she put on her mask.

“Yes. It should be quite comfortable to ride.” Lili did the same.

The moment they spoke, two dark figures appeared in the middle of the wide road. The carriage driver’s heart lurched sharply when he saw the sudden silhouettes. He immediately assumed it was a robbery.

After steadying himself slightly, he whipped the reins and accelerated straight toward them. In situations like this, running them over required no compensation!

Just as he believed the speeding carriage would send the two black-clad figures flying, the beasts pulling the carriage skidded to an abrupt stop. Their bodies trembled uncontrollably, as if they had encountered a natural predator.

“To Aureole Town, for two passengers.” At the same time, Yae-hime tossed over a small pouch of coins, which landed squarely on the panic-stricken driver’s lap.

+++

# **744 – More… More… More…**

Just as Yae-hime and Lili boarded the luxurious beast-drawn carriage and set off toward Aureole Town near Aoma Village.

· **Elsewhere, in the southern seas of Cathay. Doom Island.**

That was how the surrounding nations referred to this island of unknown ownership. Because this island truly lived up to the name. The island was thick with trees and infested with countless venomous insects. All of them were highly aggressive, and a single bite or two could send anyone with weaker resistance straight to the grave.

A place this dangerous naturally attracted almost no visitors. Even fugitives avoided it like the plague. Fishermen from nearby countries refused to approach it at all, so the island remained in a completely untouched, primordial state.

Yet on this terrifying island, a voice suddenly echoed.

“Peace to you, Matriarch.”

Deep within a cavern on Doom Island, a woman in a crimson dress knelt on one knee with her head lowered in reverence.

Before her floated a strange creature. She looked almost human, yet she possessed butterfly wings and delicate antennae atop her head.

At that moment, this beautiful being who was clearly not human slowly opened her eyes. It was a pair of eyes shimmering with multicolored light. With her awakening, the cavern grew eerily silent. The enormous insects within froze completely, as if time itself had halted.

“Red.” The butterfly-like beauty parted her cherry lips and called the woman’s name. Her voice carried an ethereal, distant quality, as though it drifted from a faraway realm.

“Matriarch, waking you ahead of time is an unforgivable crime. But this matter is far too important, so I dared to…” The woman called Red lifted her head, revealing her exquisite face.

Who else could she be but the very same Sister Red who had nearly ruined Yaeger’s life?

“Speak.” The beautiful butterfly being replied without expression. There was no telling what she was thinking.

“Matriarch, I discovered a strange creature in Cathay.” Even though the other party remained expressionless, Red knew she was already displeased. She immediately got straight to the point.

She opened the black backpack beside her and took out a square glass container. Inside was a large green cockroach on the verge of death.

The moment the butterfly being saw the cockroach, her eyes suddenly widened, and she raised a slender hand. In the next instant, the glass container was pulled toward her.

Sensing danger, the dying green cockroach suddenly writhed with desperate vigor, like a final burst of life. Unfortunately, no matter how it thrashed, it could not break the specially made glass container.

In the blink of an eye, the beautiful butterfly being was holding the container in her hand, her multicolored eyes studying the green cockroach intently.

The creature had already gone still, trembling all over. Instinct told it that this butterfly creature was unimaginably dangerous.

“Mutation.” After observing it for a moment, the butterfly being spoke. Her voice carried a trace of unmistakable surprise.

“Yes. That is why I rushed it back for you to examine,” Red replied.

“Not natural. Artificial,” the butterfly being said again. Red simply remained quiet and listened. “Interesting. A special human.”

As she spoke, multicolored light shot from the butterfly being’s eyes and pierced through the glass, striking the green cockroach with perfect precision. The cockroach tried to dodge, but its body refused to move. Within moments, it was engulfed in the multicolored radiance. Then its mind went blank.

“Bathroom… woman…” the butterfly being murmured softly. She was using a special method to search its memories. Unfortunately, she retrieved only vague fragments. No matter how mutated it was, it was still a cockroach, and its memory capacity was pitifully limited.

“Find her. Bring her back,” the butterfly being commanded.

“Yes, Matriarch,” Red lowered her head and answered. She then remembered something and added, “Matriarch, regarding the high-quality human males needed by the Broodmother, I have located a few. But she seems displeased with them.”

“Continue searching,” the butterfly being said in her calm, indifferent tone. With those words, she closed her eyes and drifted into slumber.

The glass container holding the green cockroach continued floating in midair. Seeing this, Red rose carefully, retrieved the container, and slowly backed out of the area.

Once she retreated more than ten meters away, a radiant, multicolored barrier appeared around the beautiful butterfly being, sealing her off from the outside world. At the same time, rustling sounds echoed from deeper within the cavern as the enormous insects stirred back to life.

Red left the cave and stepped outside.

Under the moonlight, she could see the cluster of giant insects gathered around the cave entrance. Some were emerald green, others glimmered with rainbow hues. Every one of them looked unmistakably venomous.

Yet despite their terrifying appearance and aggressive nature, none of them attacked her. Instead, they scattered in every direction as if fleeing from a natural predator. Unbothered by the reaction of the surrounding insects, Red suddenly lifted her gaze to the sky and muttered to herself, “Finding that special human in Roc City will not be easy.”

It was like searching for a needle in the ocean. Fortunately, she still had a clue to follow. Lowering her head, she looked at the still-trembling green cockroach in her hand and smiled. “From here on, it all depends on your performance.”

As if it understood her words, the green cockroach trembled even harder.

---

· **Inside the game.**

A luxurious beast-drawn carriage sped along the road. Despite its high speed, the passengers inside barely felt any bumps.

“This feels much better than before.” Lili lay on Yae-hime’s lap and spoke softly.

“You get what you pay for,” Yae-hime replied with a smile.

The carriage they took to the Phantabeast Range earlier had been the fastest one in Aoma Village. But speed was its only merit. Its comfort level had been terrible.

This specially modified luxury carriage, its body engraved with various inscriptions, was naturally far more comfortable than the special-express beast carriage from Aoma Village.

“Are you worried those Apostles will come looking for trouble?” Lili turned to her and asked.

Yae-hime nodded. “The Apostle you killed claimed to be the Fifth Apostle. Judging from what these Apostles said, it seems that the smaller the number, the stronger they are. Which means at least four Apostles stronger than her may come after us.”

“Yes. With your current strength, handling one Apostle stronger than that woman is possible. Any more than that becomes dangerous,” Lili said.

“That is why I asked you to help me,” Yae-hime said with a smile.

“Only to help?” Lili protested with dissatisfaction.

Yae-hime thought for a moment. “And for beauty care.”

Hearing that, Lili immediately showed a ‘now that sounds more acceptable’ expression.

‘Beauty care… because of the rush, I still have not adjusted Alicia’s body. Forget it. I will do it next time when I get the chance. It is not urgent anyway.’ With that thought, Yae-hime smiled faintly and reached out to gently pat Lili’s head.

The little one instantly squinted her eyes in bliss, shouting in her heart, ‘More, more, more~’

Unfortunately, Yae-hime only stroked her briefly before withdrawing her hand. The beast-drawn carriage continued racing forward at high speed, bringing them closer and closer to Aureole Town.

+++

# **745 – Encroaching Darkness**

At the same time. In Aoma Village, atop the watchtower.

“Angelica, look toward the deserted island!”A sturdy, dark-skinned young man pointed at the distant view captured by magic and shouted.

In the projected image, a massive shape lay sprawled across the small island that fishermen usually used for angling and drying their nets. Under the moonlight, they could only make out its vague outline, something that looked like a monster.

Staring at the image before him, the stocky young man trembled from head to toe. His lips parted and closed several times before he finally forced out two halting syllables, “Sea… beast!”

“How could a sea beast appear in coastal waters?” Angelica asked in confusion. Normally, the mana concentration near the shore was too low to attract magibeasts, let alone a large sea beast.

“If—if that isn’t a sea beast, then what is it?!” The young man’s panic grew. Having a sea beast appear near the docks would be a catastrophe. No one could predict whether it might suddenly attack nearby villages or towns.

“Perhaps a giant whale got stranded,” Angelica said with a calm expression, though unease stirred faintly in her heart. “I’m going out to confirm it.” For the villagers’ safety, she decided to head to the deserted island and see for herself.

If it really was a beached whale, it would actually benefit the villagers by providing food. But if it was a sea beast… that would be an unimaginable disaster. No matter what, she needed to confirm it first before deciding on a plan.

“You’re heading out now!?” the young man exclaimed in shock.

“Yes. I won’t feel at ease unless I see it with my own eyes,” Angelica replied with a nod. She was the village chief’s daughter and had the responsibility to protect the villagers. She could not ignore such a potential threat.

“I—I’ll stay here and continue watching…” the young man said, face paling. He didn’t dare get anywhere near that giant creature.

“Alright.” Angelica nodded, not forcing him. She left the watchtower and hurried to the church’s warehouse to inform Layna and the others. Then she set off with the best swimmers among the fishermen.

“This is far too risky! What if that suspicious sea-beast-like creature suddenly becomes hostile…” Aurora said worriedly.

“It is risky, but if we don’t figure out what it is, the villagers will remain anxious,” Layna replied.

“Even though I want to go check as well, my duty is to protect all of you,” Fiat said, sounding somewhat regretful.

“I hope Princess returns soon.” Layna glanced toward the warehouse entrance, her heart prickling with unease.

Neither she nor Aurora were combat personnel. If they followed Angelica out to sea, they would only drag her down. The only one with real fighting ability was Fiat, and he couldn’t leave because of them.

“Yes, when Princess is around… everything feels safe.” Aurora nodded. She had an inexplicable confidence in Yae-hime, for it felt like she could solve any problem just by being present.

At the docks. Angelica and five fishermen boarded a fishing boat and headed toward the deserted island.

At night, the ocean felt deep and foreboding. The orange glow of the lantern rocked softly, illuminating the faint terror on everyone’s faces, all of them uneasy. They desperately hoped that massive thing was just an ordinary marine creature and not a sea beast capable of devastating destruction.

Having just survived a horrifying plague, the last thing they wanted was another catastrophe.

Under the moonlight, the fishing boat slowly approached the deserted island. The enormous silhouette grew clearer and clearer, and as they drew nearer, its appearance gradually came into full view.

The gigantic creature looked part fish and part serpent, its body covered in scales, with four thick, powerful limbs. No matter how one looked at it, it was nothing like a whale. This was…

“Sea beast!” One of the fishermen fell straight onto the deck, shouting in terror. The moment he yelled, panic rippled through all of them, bursting forth uncontrollably.

Meanwhile, the fish-serpent beast suddenly snapped its eyes open. Its eyeballs rolled wildly, and its face twisted into a distinctly humanlike expression of pain. A pain so clear that anyone could see it.

It seemed to be enduring some kind of torment.

“Roar!” Suddenly, the fish-serpent creature let out a deafening bellow, as if it could no longer endure the pain. Right after, its massive body thrashed violently, churning the surrounding seawater into chaos.

“Not good! We need to leave immediately!” Angelica shouted. She understood that the creature wasn’t attacking them, but the waves created by its wild convulsions were more than enough to sink their boat.

Panic erupted on deck. The fishermen didn’t even hear her words. And even if some did, their trembling bodies couldn’t respond.

A surge of waves rose and came crashing down on the fishing boat! In the next instant, the boat completely shattered.

---

Outside Aureole Town, a luxurious beast-drawn carriage stood parked.

From inside the carriage, two figures stepped out. The moment they had walked several meters away, the coachman snapped the reins and fled the scene with his beast in a panicked hurry.

He had been properly paid, but fear was still fear. If he didn’t run now, was he supposed to stay and keep trembling here?

“So timid, yet he still drives night routes,” Yae-hime said with a helpless laugh as she watched the carriage speed away.

“Life is hard,” Lili replied.

“Yes.” Yae-hime smoothed her expression and looked towards the direction of Aoma Village.

There were two reasons she chose to get off here. First, she wanted to check on Aureole Town’s situation. Second, she wanted to avoid exposing her whereabouts.

The villagers of Aoma Village saw her as a so-called “Lord Angel” and naturally wouldn’t connect her to the infamous imperial scourge. But outside the village, someone as suspicious-looking as her could easily attract unwanted speculation.

“Let’s sneak into the church and see what’s going on,” Yae-hime said, withdrawing her gaze and turning toward Aureole Town’s modest walls.

“Yes. Let’s wrap this up quickly,” Lili nodded.

Those Apostles could arrive at any moment, they couldn’t afford to waste time here.

Ten minutes later. Two black silhouettes slipped out of Aureole Town and landed beside the road.

“That priest named Micha was practically a scammer in holy robes,” Lili said speechlessly.

“He is a scammer,” Yae-hime laughed.

Right now, Aureole Town’s church was even more fanatical than the one in Aoma Village. Priests and regular townsfolk alike, anyone who had witnessed a so-called _miracle_, became unbearably devout, endlessly shouting praise to the goddess.

Anyone who didn’t know better would think they had gone mad.

“I don’t believe in any of that,” Lili said coldly, shaking her head.

“I didn’t believe either.” Yae-hime gazed up at the moon hanging in the sky.

“Then why do you believe now?” Lili asked curiously.

“A secret,” Yae-hime said, turning toward her with a breathtaking smile glowing under the moonlight.

“…”

Lili’s hand flew to her chest as her heart thrashed violently. She tried to suppress it, her expression tightening with sudden pain. ‘Oh no… I’m dying… this hurts…’

How could someone be allowed to be this beautiful!? At that moment, Yae-hime’s elegant silhouette filled Lili’s mind and vision completely. There was no room left for anything else.

“It’s getting late. Let’s go back.” Yae-hime extended a slender, alabaster hand toward her, smiling gently.

Lili froze for a moment, then slowly reached out and held it. In that instant, she felt as though she was holding not just Yae-hime’s hand, but her own future.

+++

# **746 – Isn’t It Common Knowledge That Angels Can Walk on Water?**

“Emergency, emergency!”

The quiet peace of Aoma Village was suddenly shattered by a frantic shout. Many villagers hurriedly opened their doors and windows to see what was going on. They saw a sturdy, dark-skinned youth sprinting through the street while shouting, “Something terrible’s happened! Angelica and the others are in trouble!”

“What!?”

“How could anything happen inside the village?”

“Don’t tell me those damned outsiders barged in again?!”

“If they dare come, we must teach them a proper lesson this time!”

In an instant, the whole crowd was riled up, voices surging like a rising tide. However, the young man’s next words made their fiery spirits instantly collapse.

“It wasn’t outsiders. Angelica and the others went out to sea to investigate that deserted island. They ran into what might be a sea beast. They were sunk by the waves it created!”

The youth might have been panicking, but his words remained clear and steady. As soon as he finished, the square fell into absolute silence. Everyone froze as if time itself had stopped; not a single person even blinked.

After several seconds, chaos erupted completely.

“A s-sea beast!” one villager cried out first.

Panic spread like wildfire. Someone immediately bolted back into their home and locked every door and window. Someone screamed in sheer terror. Someone’s legs went weak as fear drained the color from their face. Someone stood utterly stunned, not knowing how to react at all. Someone remembered the nightmares of being at the mercy of a sea beast.

In no time, the terrifying news had spread throughout the entire village.

“Let’s go check the docks!” In the church warehouse, Layna spoke anxiously.

“Yes, big brother, let’s go!” Aurora turned to Fiat, her expression filled with worry and fear.

Fiat hesitated briefly before making a decision. “Alright. But first we need to inform the people at the church so Princess won’t worry when she returns.”

He and Angelica were not exactly close, they barely exchanged five sentences between them. But she served by Princess’ side. No matter what, he had to help.

‘I can only let them check the docks. I absolutely can’t allow them to go out to sea.’ He was deeply afraid Aurora and Layna would rush off toward that deserted island. After all, there was a terrifying creature out there that might very well be a sea beast.

Before long, they set out together with the villagers heading outside to investigate. Just as they left Aoma Village, two black shadows slipped into the village behind them.

Seeing the lights blazing and the streets packed with people, Yae-hime immediately sensed something was wrong. After overhearing the villagers’ frantic discussions and seeing the panic in their expressions, her heart sank.

“It seems something serious happened,” Lili whispered.

“They said a sea beast attacked,” Yae-hime replied, her brows tightening. It wasn’t an Apostle, but a sea beast. Something she had never expected.

“Angelica won’t be harmed, right? She’s such a good child… may the Goddess protect her!” A woman nearby prayed anxiously.

“What happened to Angelica?” Hearing her, Yae-hime quickly stepped closer and asked urgently.

“Ah—It’s the Lord Angel!” The woman was so moved she nearly fell to her knees.　　

“What exactly happened?” Yae-hime gestured for her to calm down and explain quickly.

“Yes, Lord Angel…” The woman repeated everything she had heard in detail.

Yae-hime’s expression shifted several times beneath her mask, worry weighing heavily in her heart.

“Let’s go take a look ourselves,” Lili suggested. She had met Angelica as well. Knowing the girl was in danger, she naturally couldn’t just ignore it.

“Yes. No time to waste!” Yae-hime nodded, tapped off the ground, and vaulted onto a rooftop before leaping toward the docks. Lili followed right behind her.

Under the moonlight, the villagers watched that familiar figure and couldn’t hold back their excitement as they shouted emotionally.

“It’s the Lord Angel!”

“We’re saved!”

“The Lord Angel will definitely defeat the sea beast and bring them back!”

“We’re counting on you, Lord Angel!”

“May the Goddess bless you!”

At that moment, the villagers’ fear gradually faded, replaced by a sense of relief. They firmly believed that the almighty Lord Angel could save Aoma Village a second time.

“May the Goddess bless us!”

“May the Goddess bless us!”

Right then, every villager pressed their hands together before their chest, praying devoutly to the great Goddess of Light.

“Little Hime, turns out you’re a scammer too.” Listening to the chorus of prayers, Lili said with a teasing smile.

“I’m not!” Yae-hime shot her an exasperated glare.

The two of them moved swiftly, leaving Aoma Village behind in the blink of an eye. At the same time, at the imperial docks…

“The waves are surging like crazy!” Fiat stared at the breakers slamming into the docks, utterly shocked. If the waves near the shore were already this violent, the situation at the deserted island was beyond imagination. It had to be a calamity.

Under such conditions, Angelica and the others had only the smallest chance of survival.

“Big brother, what should we do?” Aurora asked helplessly, completely lost.

“There’s nothing we can do.” Fiat shook his head.

“With waves this fierce, even seasoned fishermen wouldn’t dare enter the water, much less us.” Layna clasped her hands tightly and looked out at the pitch-black sea.

“She’s right.” Fiat nodded hard in agreement.

Seeing this, Aurora bit her lip, frustration filling her chest. When faced with true danger, she was painfully powerless. ‘If only Princess were here…’ As if responding to her wish, a strange yet familiar voice suddenly rose from behind them.

“What are you all doing here?” Even with a disguised tone, anyone who knew her could recognize it.

“Pr—” Layna turned around, about to call her name, but noticed the nearby villagers and hastily corrected herself. “You’re finally back!” Calling Yae-hime _Lord Angel_ felt impossible for her. It would make her break out in goosebumps.

Everyone looked toward the voice, faces lighting up with ecstatic joy. Hope rekindled in their hearts. As long as the Lord Angel was here, there was no such thing as a hopeless crisis.

Whether it was the villagers or Aurora and Fiat, they all trusted her completely. They believed she could overcome any obstacle and resolve this disaster.

As for Angelica and the others, saving them would, of course, be ideal. But surviving in such a vicious, raging sea was incredibly unlikely. The villagers did not hold much hope.

Aurora was about to speak when Yae-hime cut her off. “Stay here. We’ll go check the deserted island.” Before anyone could respond, Yae-hime and Lili tapped the ground lightly and leapt straight into the sea.

“Princess!” Aurora’s heart nearly jumped out of her throat.

Layna’s face went pale, and her pulse raced.

But Fiat’s sharp eyes caught something different, neither of them actually dove into the sea. They were walking on the water. ‘Amazing… what kind of realm is this!?’ Fiat balled his fists in awe.

A moment later, Aurora and Layna finally realized what they were seeing, both utterly stunned. The villagers, however, accepted it far more easily. After all, she was the Goddess’ envoy. Being able to walk on water was practically a basic skill, wasn’t it?

Seconds later, the two figures vanished entirely from everyone’s view. The sea continued to roar, like a colossal black beast awakening from slumber.

+++

# **747 – Battle Begins**

“Ha… ha…”

On the deserted island, Angelica leaned against the back of a large boulder, her face pale as she panted in pain. Her gaze dropped to her right thigh, where blood had soaked the entire area in red.

It was the wound she had sustained earlier when she leapt from the boat into the sea as the wave crashed down.

Watching her trembling leg, Angelica felt nothing but searing pain. The injury had already crippled her ability to move. Even so, surviving that monstrous wave and managing to drag herself ashore was already a stroke of luck.

“I wonder how they’re doing…” Even now, she still worried about the five villagers. At the moment she jumped, she had caught a glimpse of them fleeing in her peripheral vision.

Those villagers had spent their lives battling the sea; their survival instincts were far sharper than hers.

“I hope they’re safe.” Angelica whispered. Her soft words were instantly swallowed by the roar of the waves.

As she stared at the pitch-black sea, Angelica felt a faint twinge of regret. If she hadn’t gone out to sea, none of this would have happened. But she hadn’t had the luxury of staying behind. After all, she couldn’t allow an unknown threat to endanger Aoma Village.

Angelica wasn’t a saintess, nor a selfless martyr; she was just an ordinary girl who loved her home. Everything she said and did revealed that sentiment. At the same time, she was simply a kind, responsible, and helpful girl.

“If I were given another chance… would I still save that Apostle?” Suddenly, she recalled the Eleventh Apostle she had dragged out of the sea that day. If judged by the outcome alone, her decision that day had undoubtedly been a mistake. She shouldn’t have saved the Eleventh Apostle.

Yet such thoughts only came after the fact. Angelica had simply done what she believed was right at the time. And that was saving a life. For someone raised by the sea, such a rescue was almost instinctive, there was no time to overthink.

Unfortunately, this rescue had triggered a chain of tragic events. To this day, some people still couldn’t forgive her. As for whether Angelica regretted it… Of course she regretted it. No one ever wished for tragedy. But tragedy often struck precisely when people least expected it.

If the same thing happened again, Angelica knew she would still save the person. However, after saving them, she would never again allow them to be brought into the village.

Learning from a painful lesson didn’t mean she had to distort her principles or her will. Angelica was still growing. “I need to remember this.” she murmured. Right after that, her consciousness began to blur.

“Not good… too much blood loss…” Angelica quickly realized what was happening. Her thigh had bled far too much.

**Rumble—rrrmm!**

At that moment, the sea beast thrashed even more violently, and the entire island trembled as though it were the epicenter of an earthquake.

The intense shaking made Angelica feel unbearably ill. She could clearly feel her life slipping away at a frightening pace. These shockwaves were harmful!

In an instant, a shadow of death enveloped her, filling her with indescribable terror.

“I don’t want to die…” Angelica’s face turned even paler, the fear within her twisting into a claw of death that seemed to seize her from behind.

“Relax. With me here, you’ll never die.” Suddenly, a clear, soothing voice rang out, smashing that deathly claw like a heavy hammer.

“Princess!” Without even looking, Angelica knew exactly who that voice belonged to.

“It’s me. You’re safe now.”

“I’m here too.”

Under the beautiful moonlight, two figures appeared, one tall and one small. It was Yae-hime and Lili, who had rushed over from the docks.

With no one else around, both she and Lili had removed the masks that usually obstructed their vision. Both wore calm expressions, showing not even a trace of fatigue. It was clear that walking across the waves from the docks had cost them almost no effort at all.

“Princess… and Lady Lili!” When Angelica saw them, the terror in her heart immediately turned into overwhelming joy.

“It’s such a relief that you’re safe.” Yae-hime let out a relieved smile, then flicked a green needle that embedded itself into Angelica’s wounded thigh. In the next instant, a surge of vigorous life force flowed into her, rapidly mending her flesh and replenishing her strength.

“You really made us worry.” Lili walked over and gently tapped Angelica on the head.

Angelica froze for a moment, then her heart filled with warmth. There was no mistaking it, Lili had truly been worried about her. And that light tap on the head instantly brought their relationship much closer.

“The villagers who came with you don’t seem to be nearby.” Yae-hime scanned the surroundings, her tone calm. The only reason she had been able to locate Angelica so quickly in the vast ocean was because Angelica still carried traces of her life energy. As long as the distance wasn’t too great, she could sense it instantly.

As for the five villagers, there was no way to find them for now.

“They’re very good swimmers. They should be fine.”

Seeing the concern in Yae-hime’s eyes, Angelica spoke to reassure her.

“Mm. We need to take care of that big one first before we search for anyone else.”

The coastal waters were completely thrown into chaos by the sea beast. Relying solely on eyesight to find people would be as difficult as reaching the heavens.

“Thick hide and tough flesh. A troublesome one,” Lili said as she looked at the sea beast twisting in the distance.

“Mm. We’ll likely have to drive it back.” Yae-hime nodded.

Even working together, she and Lili would have a hard time killing this sea beast. Its health and defenses were simply too high. Wearing it down would take an entire day and still might not be enough.

But killing it was never their goal. As long as they forced it out of the coastal waters, the village would no longer be threatened. After that, they could retrieve the five villagers and complete the mission perfectly.

“Mm!” Angelica nodded strongly. She very clearly understood she was only a burden here. Following along would only hinder them.

“Let’s go.” Lili clenched her small fists, looking unusually serious.

“This is my first time fighting such a huge sea beast. I’m a little excited.” As Yae-hime spoke, she drew out the replica of the Sword of Eternity.

“It’ll be good experience.” With that, Lili tapped the ground lightly with her toes and shot forward.

Yae-hime followed right behind her.

Watching their figures rush toward the sea beast, Angelica felt a wave of longing wash over her. Her heart brimmed with excitement, and yearning. “If only I could fight alongside them…”

At the same time, Yae-hime and Lili had already arrived before the sea beast. This massive creature—part fish, part serpent, and built with thick limbs—continued thrashing its body as its heavy, pitch-black tail churned the sea relentlessly.

Its face contorted into a disturbingly human-like expression of pain, as though it were being tormented by some terrible affliction.

“Let me ask first, can you leave this sea area immediately?” Yae-hime held her sword in her right hand and stood tall like a spear as she addressed the creature. What answered her was a ferocious, sweeping claw!

+++

# **748 – I Am the King of the Coastal Seas!**

The world went dark before their eyes.

Before the massive claw could even descend, an overwhelming pressure of wind had already crashed down from above.

Yae-hime and Lili felt as if a small mountain were slamming toward them at terrifying speed. Neither of them dared hesitate. They stomped off the ground at the same time, flashing away to the left and right like bolts of lightning.

In the next instant, the gigantic claw smashed down with a thunderous boom, cracking the earth apart as shards of stone exploded into the air.

Had that strike landed on a human body, it would have pulverized it into a mist of blood.

Unfortunately, no matter how powerful an attack was, if it failed to hit its target, it was nothing more than wasted force.

Yae-hime stood atop a massive boulder, her right hand raising her sword while her left clenched two Holy Spirit Shards, her cherry lips parting softly, “Holy Spirit Power, Holy Spirit Armor, full release.”

Before her words had even faded, the two Holy Spirit Shards in her hand erupted with blinding golden radiance. The light immediately wrapped around her body, transforming into a pillar of brilliance that shot straight into the heavens.

At that moment, everyone on the docks was utterly captivated by the radiant pillar. Even from far away, they could clearly sense that familiar sacred power.

“It’s the Lord Angel!”

“The Lord Angel is fighting that sea beast!”

“Lord Angel, you can do it!”

“May the Goddess bless you!”

In an instant, the crowd erupted with fervor, a wave of fanatic excitement spreading uncontrollably.

Layna and the others decisively moved farther away, afraid of being swept up by the contagious enthusiasm.

On the uninhabited island, the pillar of light faded, revealing a maiden clad in golden holy armor, her presence akin to a valkyrie descended from legend.

It was Yae-hime, empowered by two Holy Spirit Shards. At this moment, her strength had been pushed to its absolute peak. In fact, it was not over yet. She took out a bottle of crimson potion and tilted her head back, swallowing it in one go.

The instant she finished drinking, Lili felt Yae-hime’s life aura abruptly drop by half. Yet her combat power surged upward in a violent explosion! Only now had Yae-hime reached her true strongest state.

Lili withdrew her gaze. Even as surprise flickered through her eyes, a pair of chakram materialized in her hands.

Her nickname was Dual Axe Lili. In truth, her greatest mastery lay with the twin chakrams. The axes were nothing more than a disguise. When she wielded the chakrams, that was when she was at her strongest.

“Lili, end this quickly!” Yae-hime pointed her long sword, now fully dyed gold by holy light, straight at the sea beast. Her strongest state could not last long. She could not afford for the battle to drag on.

“Exactly what I was thinking.” Lili nodded lightly as a violent aura surged out from her small body, instantly condensing into pitch-black battle armor.

On the other side, the sea beast endured the searing pain wracking its body and, for the first time, truly regarded these two tiny beings before it.

No, at this moment, they were no longer ants. They were two sea beasts of the same rank as itself. A sharp sense of danger flooded its heart. The fish-serpent sea beast threw its head back and roared, its mouth opening wide as powerful soundwaves burst outward, blasting sand and stone in all directions.

It was as if a Category Twelve typhoon had swept through the area. Yet no matter how fierce its roar was, it failed to make the two of them budge even a step.

Formidable enemies. They were absolutely formidable enemies. The sea beast’s eyes widened abruptly as a column of pressurized water erupted from its mouth.

Only then did Yae-hime and Lili finally move. With a light tap of their toes, they instantly evaded the incoming high-pressure water jet.

In the next breath, they stepped onto the air itself, weapons in hand, and charged toward their foe at breakneck speed.

The high-pressure water column drilled straight into the ground, punching through the rocky surface with a deafening crash and leaving behind a massive cavern. That single strike was terrifyingly powerful. But again, an attack that missed was utterly meaningless.

Yae-hime gripped her sword with both hands and raised it high overhead as golden light blossomed along the blade. Lily’s chakrams flashed, black radiance flickering across their edges. The two launched their attacks in perfect unison.

Yae-hime’s sword cleaved down from above, golden light flooding the sky like a celestial river pouring down from the Ninth Heavens. Lili’s chakrams danced as jet-black energy erupted in full, surging upward like a chasm spewing forth abyssal power.

One was light. One was darkness.

Powers that should have stood in opposition instead fused flawlessly together, crashing down upon the sea beast in an overwhelming deluge. In that split second, a colossal explosion erupted, shaking both sky and sea.

Light and darkness detonated together, the violent shockwave expanding like a stellar halo and sweeping every loose object on the uninhabited island clean into the air.

If the fish-serpent sea beast’s roar had been a Category Twelve typhoon, then Yae-hime and Lili’s combined strike was nothing less than a Category Twelve tornado.

At this very moment, even the sea itself was forcibly carved into a spiraling vortex by the shockwave.

“Ah!” Angelica clung desperately to the cracks in the rock, struggling to withstand the residual impact, her body wracked with agony.

“Roar!” At the same time, an enraged bellow burst forth from the center of the explosion.

It was clear that the fish-serpent sea beast had not perished under the combined strike of Yae-hime and Lili.

Neither of them showed any surprise on their faces. Trying to eliminate this sea beast with just that single attack had always been wishful thinking. Everything was proceeding exactly as expected.

The dust was swiftly blown away, revealing the fish-serpent sea beast covered in wounds. Its once-proud scales had fallen away in large patches, emerald-green blood continuously spilling out and turning the massive crater into a pool. A foul, fishy stench spread through the air, enough to make one retch.

It stared at Yae-hime and Lili floating in midair, its eyes shot through with bloodshot veins, its grotesque face twisted into an unmistakably human expression of rage. The fish-serpent sea beast was truly furious.

As a sea beast, it should have been the undisputed king of these coastal seas. Unrivaled. Yet these two unknown intruders had driven it into such a miserable state.

Shame. Rage. Hatred. Resentment. Just as it was about to vent this storm of emotions, Yae-hime had already shot downward like an arrow loosed from a bow.

Lili followed closely behind, the chakrams in her hands flashing with piercing, icy radiance.

Seeing the two closing in at high speed, the fish-serpent sea beast felt both angered and amused. These tiny creatures actually dared to engage it in close combat. It was nothing short of laughable!

(I will let you witness the true power of the King of the Coastal Seas!)

Its grotesque face seemed to radiate that very message.

Yae-hime had no way of understanding whatever it was trying to convey. Gripping her sword with both hands, she struck down immediately like a bolt of thunder.

The Sword of Eternity replica, its blade gleaming with golden light, drove its sharp tip viciously into the exposed flesh where the fish-serpent sea beast had lost the protection of its scales.

Immense holy power poured in without restraint, flooding its body in a violent surge.

At that moment, the fish-serpent sea beast felt as if its entire head were about to explode. That power behaved almost like a living thing, launching a ferocious assault within its body, especially concentrated around its head.

It experienced an excruciating agony as if every nerve were being severed one by one.

“Roar!” The fish-serpent sea beast let out a shrill, miserable howl, then rolled its enormous body, attempting to crush Yae-hime beneath its bulk.

Sensing its intent, Yae-hime immediately yanked her sword free, kicked off its body, and leapt high into the air.

At the same time, the fish-serpent sea beast’s back slammed heavily into the ground, making the entire island shudder as if struck by a violent earthquake.

But it was not finished yet. It swiftly flipped over, and its long, thick black tail whipped up a towering wave, hurling it toward Yae-hime and the Lili who was about to seize the opening to attack!

The two exchanged a glance and nodded in unison, their figures flashing. They actually charged straight into the massive wave.

With a deafening boom, the wave that blotted out the sky crashed violently onto the uninhabited island, causing an even more intense tremor than before.

Angelica immediately spat out a mouthful of blood as her body suffered heavy damage. Fortunately, the life energy Yae-hime had left within her was still abundant and quickly healed her injuries.

“What kind of terrifying battle is this, exactly…” Supporting herself against the rocky cliff, she looked toward the distant battlefield that had been reduced to utter ruin, her expression filled with shock as she spoke.

+++

# **749 – The Defeated Sea Beast and the Mysterious Object**

At this moment, the terrain cracked apart and the sea surged violently, the intense tremors seeming ready to tear the small island apart entirely.

The ground where Angelica stood was relatively higher, yet seawater still flooded past her knees, the raging current making it difficult for her to keep her footing.

This was a natural disaster. For those who lived along the coast, sea beasts were walking natural disasters. Now, this fish-serpent sea beast was displaying precisely that terrifying power.

“Princess… Lady Lili…” Angelica clung to a crevice in the rocks, barely managing to support her body as she looked ahead with worry shining in her beautiful eyes.

Within the shattered battlefield, the fish-serpent sea beast stared wide-eyed, its berserk aura surging uncontrollably. Its mind was stretched taut, its eyeballs rolling restlessly as though it were searching for something.

Suddenly, with a violent splash, two figures, one large and one small, leapt out of the sea. It was Yae-hime and Lili.

Yae-hime’s eyes sharpened as she thrust forward a fully charged sword strike, golden light exploding outward in an instant and completely dispelling the surrounding darkness.

Lili swung her chakrams, forming a sky-covering black curtain that split the battlefield evenly with the holy radiance.

Seeing this, the fish-serpent sea beast reacted at once, its entire body tensing as its scales shifted into a purplish-red hue.

In the next instant, two overwhelming attacks slammed into its body, and the third wave of impact erupted in full force.

The seawater that had surged up earlier was blasted away and forced back into the ocean. Shattered rocks shot out in all directions, riddling the surroundings with countless holes.

Angelica hid behind a rock, gripping the cracks tightly with both hands as she forced herself to stay steady. Her face flushed slightly, her entire body trembling. Even from such a distance, she was affected. One could only imagine how horrifying this battle truly was.

When the aftershocks finally faded, salty rain fell from the sky.

The raindrops pattered against the massive purplish-red body, producing a steady drip-drip sound. It actually looked completely unscathed.

Yae-hime and Lili stood suspended in midair, each holding their weapon, their expressions icy and severe.

The fish-serpent sea beast glared at them in fury, yet its heart trembled with fear. Even after activating its hardening ability, its internal organs had still suffered considerable damage from those two strikes. For now, it merely appeared unharmed on the surface.

If possible, it truly wanted to flee at once. However, as a king, how could it retreat? Even if it retreated, it had to do so with honor. That’s right. It absolutely could not flee in disgrace.

At that moment, a piercing, twisting pain surged up from its abdomen, causing the fish-serpent sea beast to reveal an extremely human-like expression of agony.

Seeing such a glaring opening, how could Yae-hime and Lili possibly let this perfect opportunity slip by? The two immediately unleashed a near-maniacal assault, beating the fish-serpent sea beast until it let out pitiful, shrill cries.

Fortunately, its hide was thick and its flesh tough, its defensive power astonishing. Otherwise, within just a few seconds, Lili and Yae-hime could have sent it straight to its doom.

At this very moment, the fish-serpent sea beast was wracked with unbearable pain both inside and out, so nauseated it felt like vomiting. It could only thrash its massive body wildly, attempting to fight back.

However, Yae-hime and Lili were incredibly agile, darting and shifting with effortless ease. They attacked like a raging storm while dodging at the same time, maintaining relentless pressure without pause.

The beating shattered the sea beast’s will to fight, leaving it no longer concerned with any so-called royal honor. Unfortunately for it, under the pair’s ferocious assault, it struggled even to stand firm, let alone retreat.

Sensing that the timing was right, Yae-hime decisively used the third Holy Spirit Shard. At the same time, Lili unleashed the corresponding level of power. In truth, she had yet to fight at full strength until now.

On one hand, she wanted Yae-hime to experience battles of this caliber more deeply, accelerating his growth. On the other hand, she needed to conserve her strength and avoid excessive energy consumption.

After all, if anything went wrong on Alicia’s side, it would be a serious problem.

Now that the decisive moment had finally arrived, she naturally would not hold back any longer. If she could drive this sea beast back with a single blow, it would instead save a great deal of energy.

The pitiful sea beast had already wanted to retreat and stop entangling itself with them. Yet, because both sides were unable to communicate, it had been helplessly beaten down ever since. It could not have been more miserable.

Lili’s chakrams merged into one, a flash of icy blue killing intent passing through her eyes. Jet-black energy erupted from within her body like a volcanic explosion, surging violently outward.

At once, an overwhelming sense of danger welled up in the fish-serpent sea beast’s heart. It forced the creature to momentarily forget the agony wracking its body and focus all its attention on facing the terrifying strike that was about to come.

No, not one strike, but two.

Yae-hime clenched the sword hilt with both hands as sacred power poured into the blade as though it cost her nothing.

In an instant, night turned into day, and dazzling golden radiance burst forth.

From the distant docks, people looked on as if they were gazing at a golden sun. It was blindingly brilliant, overwhelmingly sacred, and utterly untouchable.

Knees weakening, some villagers fell to the ground, devoutly clasping their hands to their chests while murmuring prayers. One became two, then more and more, until villagers across the area knelt down in succession, fervently praying for something unknown.

The sight made Layna and the others’ eyes and mouths twitch faintly. They truly could not understand such behavior. Nor could they comprehend the feverish, fanatical atmosphere permeating the surroundings.

**Boom!**

Suddenly, a thunderous explosion rang out from afar.

Everyone followed the sound and faintly saw a pillar of black light slam into the sea beast, sending it hurtling upward.

That massive body was actually blasted into the air.

At the same time, the golden sun rapidly contracted, all its brilliance condensing into a single point. Immediately after, Yae-hime thrust her sword forward. Heaven and sea alike were dyed in radiant gold at that very moment. Sacred power spread outward. It was as though a god were bestowing holy blessings upon the world below.

Only the fish-serpent sea beast sensed the unprecedented danger. It felt like the claws of death had seized its heart without mercy. In the blink of an eye, its body was engulfed by sacred light.

A sharp aura of destruction stabbed into its unguarded abdomen, bringing tearing agony that racked its entire body.

The fish-serpent sea beast’s insides churned violently as it threw open its enormous jaws and spewed out everything it had eaten over the past few days. The sight was so extreme it looked as if it wanted to vomit out its very organs.

Amid the expelled mess, Yae-hime faintly caught sight of a glowing object shooting toward the deserted island.

At that moment, the full might of the sacred sword was unleashed, blasting the fish-serpent sea beast’s gigantic body straight away.

It should have been excruciating, yet its expression instead resembled that of a middle-aged man finally relieved of severe constipation, wearing a look of unexpected bliss.

Right after that, it plunged into the deep sea, smashing down and raising towering waves.

“Haa… this thing really is ridiculously tough,” Yae-hime let out a light breath, her face filled with exhaustion. She knew full well that her strike could not kill the fish-serpent sea beast. At best, she had only dealt it a heavy blow.

“Mm. Killing it would take quite some time,” Lili nodded, her condition far better than Yae-hime’s, clearly with strength still to spare.

“I wonder if it’ll retreat after this,” Yae-hime said worriedly. That last attack had nearly drained her dry. If the fish-serpent sea beast insisted on continuing the fight, it would have to be Lili who carried on.

“I don’t think it will fight anymore,” Lili replied.

As if responding to her words, the fish-serpent sea beast surfaced, letting out sounds that oddly carried a hint of cheerfulness as it swam toward the open sea. It truly seemed unwilling to continue the battle.

Yae-hime could not help but let out a sigh of relief, then turned her gaze toward the place where the glowing object had flown earlier.

“Lili, it looks like we’ve picked up a real treasure.”

At that moment, light blossomed there, and a mysterious aura slowly spread through the air.

+++

# **750 – BZZT—BZZT~~~**

The sea surface gradually returned to calm.

Lili and Yae-hime landed on the island together, their gazes turning toward the glowing object not far away.

With light, measured steps, the two approached it. The closer they got, the more intense the mysterious aura became. At the same time, there was another powerful presence, faint yet unmistakable.

Toward this presence, Yae-hime felt an inexplicable sense of closeness.

“I’m sensing danger,” Lili said softly, her expression solemn.

“Really?” Yae-hime blinked, asking in confusion. She clearly did not sense anything similar.

“It feels like something extremely dangerous is wrapped inside,” Lili nodded, her expression growing even more serious.

“….” Yae-hime felt even more puzzled by that statement. ‘There is a very obvious gap between Lili and me in terms of strength, but when it comes to perception, there shouldn’t be such a big difference…’

With a Luck value of 666, her sensitivity to danger far surpassed that of ordinary people. At times, she could even foresee danger before it happened.

“That sea beast probably appeared in the sea shore waters because of this thing.” Recalling the fish-serpent sea beast’s earlier agony, then combining it with how it had fled in apparent relief, Lili arrived at that conclusion.

Yae-hime strongly agreed with her. After all, under normal circumstances, why would a sea beast willingly come to such a barren area with sparse mana?

“It probably thought it was something tasty and swallowed it,” Yae-hime said with a wry smile.

If Lili had not been there today, she alone really would not have had any way to drive off that fish-serpent sea beast.

“The intense pain in its stomach made it lose its sense of direction, causing it to dash around wildly before ending up here to rest on this uninhabited island.” Lili analyzed the situation briefly and felt her guess was likely very close to the truth.

“That’s very possible. It really did look like it was in a lot of pain earlier,” Yae-hime said.

“How should we deal with this thing?” Lili frowned slightly as she looked at the glowing object.

Because it was wrapped in a sphere of light, it was impossible to see what was inside. On the outside, arcs of electricity crackled and snapped, filling the air with sharp sizzling sounds and giving her an extremely dangerous feeling.

“Why don’t we get closer and take a look?” Yae-hime suggested. She did not sense any danger at all and could basically confirm that the object was harmless to her.

Lili hesitated for a moment, then nodded in agreement, ‘With me here, it shouldn’t be a problem.’

The two cautiously approached the glowing object. Along the way, none of the dangers Lili had anticipated appeared.

At last, they stood directly in front of the glowing object. It was something shaped like a gigantic egg.

It radiated a powerful aura that made one’s heart tremble. Its surface crackled with flashing arcs of electricity, the air snapping and popping with sharp crackles as it was violently ionized.

“What are you trying to do?!” Seeing Yae-hime suddenly reach out, clearly intending to touch the lightning arcs, Lili hurriedly stopped her.

In her eyes, those lightning arcs were the most dangerous part. Far more dangerous than whatever lay inside.

“These lightning arcs contain an extremely profound power of destruction. You absolutely must not touch them!” Lili said sternly.

Hearing this, Yae-hime tilted her head slightly and asked in confusion, “But I don’t feel any danger at all. Could it be that my strength is too low, so I can’t sense it?”

“That’s possible.” As she said that, a wave of doubt surged in Lili’s heart. Those lightning arcs were openly releasing a dangerous aura. Yet her little Hime seemed to genuinely feel nothing at all…

And Lili did not believe Yae-hime was the type to be careless or dull-witted.

‘Something’s strange. There must be something strange.’ Lili raised her head and carefully studied Yae-hime. The more she looked, the more beautiful she seemed, until it became impossible to grow tired of looking.

“Is there something on my face?” Yae-hime asked, touching her cheek.

“N-no, nothing! Forget it!” Lili hurriedly turned her head away toward the glowing giant egg. “This thing is really hard to deal with. It’s giving me a headache.”

Yae-hime also looked at the glowing egg and said softly, “Then I’ll try touching it.”

Before figuring out what was inside, she truly could not feel at ease. Who knew whether this might become a new disaster? It might even be more troublesome than that sea beast. If they did not resolve it now and it suddenly erupted later, it would be far too late.

After pondering for a moment, Lili shook her head. “I’ll try first.” As soon as she finished speaking, she released Yae-hime’s hand, stepped forward, and reached out with her small hand.

Before she could even get close to the giant egg, a bolt of lightning suddenly shot out and struck her hand.

“Uwaaah!” In the next instant, the girl’s shrill cry rang out across the island.

Seeing Lili’s entire body wreathed in crackling electricity, Yae-hime acted without a second thought and rushed to help. She placed one hand on Lili’s shoulder. It was an action driven purely by instinct.

The moment that pale, jade-like hand touched her shoulder, Lili’s mind went blank with a single thought: _Oh no._

An attack she herself could barely endure was something little Hime could never withstand. Disaster felt inevitable. Yet, the outcome she feared never came. Those electric currents seemed to be irresistibly drawn toward Yae-hime, transferring entirely from Lili’s body.

They then rapidly merged into Yae-hime’s body. The entire process was extremely fast. So fast that Lili barely had time to react.

At that moment, Yae-hime only felt her body crackling, slightly uncomfortable. But that sensation lasted barely two seconds before disappearing.

What followed was a system notification. Her lightning-attribute resistance had increased. At the same time, an additional strand of profound, mysterious power appeared within her body.

“As expected, it has no effect on me,” Yae-hime said with a smile. Hearing that, and seeing her smile, Lili was completely dumbfounded, her jaw nearly dropping.

The lightning arcs that had caused her so much pain were absorbed just like that by Yae-hime. How was anyone supposed to believe that? After all, there was a huge gap in their strengths!

“How did you do that?” Lili asked in shock.

If she were not already somewhat used to Yae-hime’s astonishing feats, she would probably have been staring wide-eyed, jaw hanging open long ago.
