“It just happened naturally,” Yae-hime answered honestly.

“That’s incredible. You must have some kind of special physique!” Lili said enviously. Other than that, she could not think of any other explanation.

“My physique is indeed a bit special.” Yae-hime nodded, then turned her gaze back to the glowing giant egg. “We can talk about my physique later. For now, let’s deal with this thing first.”

“Mhm.” Lili nodded lightly. Since her little Hime was not afraid of those lightning arcs, there was nothing left to worry about.

Yae-hime reached out once more. Before her hand even touched the glowing giant egg, the lightning arcs eagerly wrapped around her body, surging and pouring into her without restraint. In the next instant, her lightning-attribute resistance skyrocketed at an astonishing rate.

At first, that crackling sensation made her feel slightly uncomfortable. But once she grew accustomed to it, it became extraordinarily pleasant. It was as if every part of her body had been activated, bringing an intense, blissful sensation. So comfortable that Yae-hime nearly let out an embarrassingly cute sound.

On the other side, Lili was completely stunned. Because the lightning arcs surrounding the glowing giant egg had been absorbed entirely by Yae-hime in the blink of an eye!

“Ah~” Finally, at the moment her lightning-attribute resistance reached its peak, the beautiful girl could not help but let out a soul-stirring cry.

+++

# **751 – A Mysterious Maiden from the East**

Looking at Yae-hime standing there with her arms crossed over her chest, her body trembling slightly, her face wearing an unmistakably blissful expression, Lili could not help but feel her eyelids twitch.

For some reason, the image of the Seventh Princess, Kastina, suddenly surfaced in her mind.

‘Little Hime has not gotten her brain fried by the lightning, right?’ The thought made her uneasy. If her Little Hime were to turn into someone like Kastina, what would she do then?

At this moment, Yae-hime felt indescribably euphoric, as though her body and soul had sunk into a river of honey, sweet and blissful beyond words. She felt as if she could take off and soar into the sky at any moment.

Just as she was about to ascend into pure bliss, her mind turning completely blank, the system’s voice rang out abruptly.

Ding! You have obtained Basic Lightning Force.

The cool, detached voice instantly yanked her soul back from midair, and her brain, which had momentarily lost all capacity for thought, slowly began functioning again.

‘Such terrifying lightning power, it nearly made me lose myself in pleasure…’ Yae-hime shuddered, a trace of lingering fear rising in her heart. If she had lost control for even a moment and exposed herself in front of Lili, it would have dealt a severe blow to her image.

Despite her usual carefree demeanor, she actually cared quite a lot about how she was perceived. A sidelong glance revealed Lili’s expression, one that was both relieved and complicated.

‘That is… rather subtle. Forget it, I will pretend I did not notice.’ Yae-hime gently closed her eyes and turned her attention inward, observing the changes within her body.

The most obvious change was her strength. Compared to before, it had increased by roughly one tenth. To gain such a significant boost without any change in level was nothing short of remarkable.

She had already been able to dominate opponents of the same level and fight above her rank. Now, she had undoubtedly become even more terrifying.

‘Hm? What is this?’ Suddenly, Yae-hime noticed a golden object the size of a marble spinning endlessly within her body. A profoundly mysterious aura seeped from it, giving her the illusion of standing at the very center of the vast cosmos.

She could clearly sense that this tiny bead concealed an astonishingly frightening amount of power. ‘Could it be that the lightning power condensed into this?’

“Little Hime, are you alright?” Lili’s worried voice cut through her thoughts.

“I am fine. Better than ever.” Yae-hime opened her eyes, a bright smile blooming across her delicate face, stunningly beautiful.

“That is good.” Lili finally relaxed her clenched fists, letting out a quiet sigh of relief. ‘Thank goodness. Little Hime did not get electrocuted into an idiot.’

If Yae-hime had known what Lili was thinking, she would have rolled her eyes without hesitation.

“There is really nothing wrong with your body?” Lili stepped closer, scrutinizing Yae-hime from head to toe.

Yae-hime sensed her condition carefully. Aside from that mysterious little bead, there was not the slightest abnormality to be found. In fact, her physical state felt so incredible that it was almost unreal.

Punching a Platinum-rank Desert Bison to death with a single blow would pose no problem at all.

“There is no issue. I am perfectly fine.” Yae-hime lowered her gaze to Lili and smiled.

She was far from indifferent toward that mysterious little bead, but there were still many matters demanding her attention. Any further investigation would have to wait.

**Crack!**

A crisp sound suddenly echoed through the area. Lili and Yae-hime tensed at once and turned toward the source. The glowing giant egg had split open, a clear fissure running across its surface.

Centered on that crack, fractures rapidly spread in all directions. Finally, with a dull bang, the entire shell shattered into pieces. In the blink of an eye, those fragments dissolved into particles of light and drifted away.

Lili and Yae-hime stared intently at the spot where the light dispersed, revealing a petite figure. She had jet-black hair, her eyes tightly closed, skin as pale and smooth as jade, and she wore a flowing pleated skirt that was somewhat tattered but clearly made of fine material.

A closer look revealed traces of burns scattered across her body. Her delicate little face was twisted in visible pain. The moment Yae-hime laid eyes on her, an inexplicable sense of closeness welled up inside.

It felt like encountering someone from home for the first time in a foreign land. No, that was not quite right. This was her own kin.

‘The Celestials… She is from the Celestial Clan!’

In an instant, she identified the girl’s race. That attire, that shared origin of aura, there was no possibility of mistake. This was the Celestial, a heaven-defying race that was not supposed to appear until more than two years later, nearly three years from now.

‘Why is a Celestial here? She should not have appeared at this time!’ Yae-hime clenched her fists, her face turning deathly pale as she stared at the little girl who looked as though she were merely asleep, her heart trembling uncontrollably.

On the other side, Lili faced the situation as if confronting a formidable enemy. Her small face was filled with severity, her nerves drawn as taut as a fully drawn bow. From this little girl, she sensed a faint yet unmistakable aura of danger. A threat great enough to endanger herself.

“Ugh!” At that moment, the little girl suddenly let out a cry of pain.

Immediately afterward, multicolored arcs of lightning surged across her body, snapping and crackling as they tore at the surrounding air.

“This is…” Seeing this, Yae-hime’s brows lifted, shock flashing across her face. Because the small bead within her body began trembling excitedly the instant lightning arcs burst from the girl.

There truly was a deep connection between the two. This Celestial maiden was clearly far from ordinary.

“She seems to be seriously injured. Perhaps she was struck by the Ninth Heaven’s Divine Lightning.” Lili unclenched her small hands, and the tension in her body eased accordingly.

With her breadth of knowledge, she had already more or less guessed the nature of the injury. On the Eastern Continent, heavenly lightning was known as the Ninth Heaven’s Divine Lightning. Only those who incurred the wrath of the heavens would be punished by such divine thunder.

This little girl must have committed some deed that angered both heaven and people alike, which was why she had ended up in such a state. Being entangled by that kind of divine lightning, staying alive could very well be more painful than death.

“This little girl should be from the Eastern Continent,” Lili continued. “Judging by the situation, she has been severely punished by the heavens.”

“A lightning tribulation eh…” Hearing the words Ninth Heaven’s Divine Lightning, Yae-hime could not help but think of the Nine Heavens Lightning Tribulation that cultivators had to face when ascending.

‘Could it be that she is a cultivator who has just gone through a tribulation, rather than a Celestials?’ The thought filled her with doubt.

In truth, Yae-hime herself could not clearly distinguish between native Celestials and those who ascended after cultivation.

‘It is not yet time for the Celestials to appear. By normal reasoning, this little girl is very likely a cultivator who has reached the point of ascension. But if that is the case… then the problem is, how could there be cultivators in this world!?’ The more she thought about it, the more something felt off.

Yet upon closer reflection, she realized there was nothing truly strange about it. This world was unimaginably vast. Even if a cultivation-based civilization existed somewhere within it, that alone was not particularly surprising.

In Yae-hime’s previous life, humanity had spent three whole years and still failed to explore even one-tenth of this world.

“Little Hime, what should we do with her?” Lili asked. If possible, she wanted to eliminate the little girl immediately. An unknown danger could not be left alive.

Yae-hime hesitated briefly, then said, “Let’s take her back and see how things turn out.”

“I think she is dangerous,” Lili warned.

“It’s fine. She is injured so badly that she won’t pose a threat to us for the time being,” Yae-hime replied calmly. Unlike Lili, she felt no sense of danger at all from the little girl. Moreover, her intuition told her that this little girl would be very useful.

+++

# **752 – I’m Not a Charlatan!**

Lili lightly bit her cherry-red lower lip, her mind racing as she considered how she might persuade Yae-hime.

That little girl was indeed gravely injured and posed no threat to them for the time being. But if her injuries were to recover… The more Lili thought about it, the heavier the worry weighing on her heart became.

Just then, a clear and pleasant voice rang out from not far away. Along with it came the sound of hurried footsteps splashing through shallow water.

“Princess, Lady Lili!”

The two of them looked over, only to see Angelica, her clothes and hair somewhat disheveled, running toward them.

“Slow down, the ground is slippery,” Yae-hime reminded her.

The uninhabited island had been thoroughly washed by the earlier waves, leaving pools of water everywhere. A single misstep or slip would surely result in a painful fall.

However, Angelica, running under the moonlight, moved steadily the entire way. It was clear that she was quite accustomed to this kind of environment.

“Princess, Lady Lili, you were incredible!” She finally reached them, and before she had even fully steadied herself, she spoke excitedly. To drive off such a terrifying sea beast in such a short time, if she had not witnessed it with her own eyes, she would never have believed it.

At this very moment, Angelica’s admiration and reverence for Yae-hime and Lili surged like an unending river.

“It had merely wandered into the nearshore while confused. Once it was knocked awake, it naturally fled,” Yae-hime said with a smile. She then explained the reason the fish-serpent sea beast had intruded into the shallow waters.

“That’s really astonishing…” Angelica said as she looked at the little girl lying on the ground, whose beauty was almost excessive. “She’s way too amazing. She actually made that sea beast suffer so badly!”

“She is indeed impressive,” Lili nodded. She still had not figured out how to persuade Yae-hime. ‘Alicia said not to interfere excessively with the Child of Destiny, but…’ Dangerous things truly could not be ignored.

Looking at the little girl’s pained expression, Lili felt deeply conflicted.

“Angelica, do you have a way to contact the dock and have them send boats over?” Yae-hime asked, turning to her.

The crisis had already been resolved, and there was no point in staying here any longer. Moreover, she wanted to return as soon as possible to conduct some research… no, to give the little girl some basic treatment.

“Little Hime, are you really going to take her back?” Lili asked anxiously.

“Yes. Don’t worry. My intuition is very accurate. She’s harmless.” Seeing the concern in Lili’s heart, Yae-hime reassured her.

At the side, Angelica’s expression looked somewhat unnatural. To her, this scene felt eerily similar to when she had rescued the apostle before. What happened afterward had left her with a deep psychological shadow.

Now that Yae-hime intended to bring back someone of unknown origin, would it also… At this thought, Angelica forcefully shook her head. ‘Princess must have absolute confidence to do this. It’s completely different from me!’

She quickly realized the vast gap between herself and Princess. Yae-hime dared to make such decisions because she had the strength to back them up. She herself lacked that ability.

If she had possessed the power to effortlessly resolve the plague in the village back then, like Yae-hime had, then none of those problems would have been problems at all. Unfortunately, she did not have such strength. That was the difference.

‘Only by possessing great power can one live freely.’ Clenching her fist lightly, Angelica finally came to an understanding. At this moment, she had grown a little more than before.

“Angelica?” Seeing that she had not replied, Yae-hime waved a hand in front of her.

“Uwah!” Angelica snapped back to her senses and jumped in fright.

“What were you thinking about so deeply?” Yae-hime asked with a smile.

“N-nothing! Oh, right. I can blow a specially made horn to send a signal to the dock!” In her fluster, Angelica fumbled in her pocket and pulled out a small black horn.

“Mhm. It’d be best if they could send two or three ships over,” Yae-hime said.

Although the crisis had been resolved, five villagers were still unaccounted for. The matter had yet to truly come to an end.

In addition, they also needed to take a boat back.

Walking atop the waves was convenient enough, but bringing people along made it far less effortless. Carrying extra weight still affected them, and hauling two people back like that would seriously hurt their image. Especially after such a grand, earthshaking battle earlier.

Yae-hime felt that this kind of contrast was not very conducive to maintaining an air of mystery. However, this was clearly overthinking it on her part. At this very moment, the dock was like a frenzied celebration, lively and feverish. After all, they had just witnessed an epic battle.

Their divine envoy had fought on behalf of the Goddess of Light, unleashing supreme divine power to drive the sea beast back out of the nearshore waters, once again restoring clear skies and calm seas to Aoma Village.

What overwhelming divine grace this was.

People at the bottom were very pragmatic. Whoever manifested miracles was the one they devoted themselves to.

After Yae-hime had turned the tide twice, the standing of the Goddess of Light in their hearts had undoubtedly skyrocketed.

Just then, a series of horn blasts rose from the distance, their long, low calls rolling across the night and cutting through the air, gradually pressing down the crowd’s surging excitement.

“Stop!” an elderly villager with considerable authority raised both hands and shouted.　

In the next moment, the villagers’ roaring voices gradually subsided until everything fell completely silent. At that point, the horn sounded again, echoing clearly.

“Three long, two short. That’s a signal of good news! Angelica and the others are safe!” the elderly villager exclaimed excitedly.

“That’s wonderful!”

“Let’s head out to sea and welcome them back at once!”

“Set out!”

In the blink of an eye, the villagers sprang into action.

“Should we go over as well?” Layna asked.

“Brother.” Aurora looked toward her older brother.

“We’d better not go and add to the chaos,” Fiat said seriously, folding his arms across his chest.

“That’s true. We wouldn’t really be able to help anyway,” Layna nodded.

Aurora thought it over and agreed, dispelling the idea of going out to sea. She obediently stayed at the dock, waiting for Yae-hime to return in triumph.

“Princess, people from the dock will be sailing over soon,” Angelica said after faintly spotting distant lights.

“Mm, thank you for your hard work,” Yae-hime said as she gently patted her head.

Beside her, Lili wore an envious expression.

After waiting for more than ten minutes, three fishing boats finally docked, and many villagers disembarked.

“Lord Angel!” someone shouted the moment they came ashore. Immediately afterward, the words resounded throughout the uninhabited island.

Behind the mask, the corner of Yae-hime’s eye twitched slightly. How could she fail to see the fanaticism in their eyes, or fail to hear the reverence in their shouts?

“Charlatan,” Lili said softly, glancing over.

“I’m not!” Yae-hime shot her a glare.

She then instructed Angelica to handle the matters that followed. She really did not want to have any direct contact with these villagers.

“All right, Prin… Lord Angel,” Angelica said, hurriedly correcting herself halfway through.

“Go on,” Yae-hime said with a light wave of her hand.

“Yes,” Angelica responded and quickly stepped forward to stop the villagers.

The top priority was to locate the five villagers who were still missing. Soon, the three boats set out once more.

After spending fifty minutes, the villagers found those five people among nearby reefs. Each of them had suffered injuries of varying severity, but fortunately, none were life-threatening. With Yae-hime’s treatment, they were immediately lively again.

At last, the matter could be considered settled. However, just as the group returned to the dock, the headache Yae-hime had anticipated indeed occurred.

“Welcome, Lord Angel!” On the dock, several hundred villagers knelt, their eyes blazing with fervor, their expressions devout, their voices rising in perfect unison.

+++

# **753 – I Really Didn’t Sign Up to Be a Lord Angel**

Watching this scene unfold, Yae-hime felt her scalp prickle, her entire body stiff with discomfort.

To her, the situation felt exactly like a beautiful girl trying cosplay for the first time at a convention, only to be stared at and visually devoured by hundreds of camera-wielding otaku.

There was no way anyone could remain natural under that kind of gaze.

It was not just Yae-hime who felt this way. Lili and the others were no different.

All around them, waves of fervent cheers rang out without pause. Praises of “Lord Angel unrivaled beneath the heavens,” “second to none among mortals,” “heaven-bestowed talent,” “chosen saint of the goddess,” and countless other exaltations filled the air.

Listening to it all, Yae-hime’s eyelids and lips twitched at the same time. This kind of frenzied personal worship was not a good sign. After all, she was not truly a divine envoy. If the Holy Empire were to take notice of her, things would become troublesome.

In this era where the gods no longer walked the world, gods themselves were cheap, and angels were even cheaper. A suddenly appearing envoy would clearly not be welcomed by the Holy Empire.

On the contrary, the more extraordinary the angel’s performance was, the more likely they were to quietly vanish from the world. Because the very existence of an angel already threatened their “divine authority.”

This was a conflict between orthodoxy and heresy. At its core, it was still a struggle over self-interest.

Yae-hime’s abrupt emergence brought nothing but harm to the church. To them, only a dead angel was a good angel. That was precisely why Yae-hime had worried from the beginning about the Holy Empire coming after her.

‘The Holy Empire is still too early for me. If I can avoid them, I should avoid them.’ She gently shook her head, then made a swift decision to shift the blame elsewhere. “Praise the Goddess!”

Suddenly, standing in place, she lifted her head toward the sky, raised both hands high, and shouted in a slightly peculiar tone. Seeing Lord Angel act this way, the crowd froze for a moment.

Then, as if infected, everyone followed suit, raising their heads and hands toward the heavens and shouting the same words.

‘Lord Angel truly lives up to being the Goddess’ chosen emissary. Every gesture radiates reverence for the Goddess!’

‘Lord Angel really is the Goddess’ most devout believer! I’m in love, I’m in love!’

‘Long live the Goddess, long live Lord Angel!’

At that moment, everyone’s inner thoughts surged wildly. Their reverence for Yae-hime was like the rolling sea, endlessly rising and falling.

If they ever found out that the pretty face beneath the mask belonged to one of the Empire’s greatest scourges, the “Black-Hearted Princess,” one could only imagine what spectacular expressions they would wear then.

Having successfully tossed the responsibility away, Yae-hime could not help but let the corner of her lips lift as she thought to herself. Naturally, she had no intention of revealing her identity anytime soon.

A hiding place as safe and convenient as Aoma Village was not easy to come by.

“I’m a little tired,” Yae-hime said calmly as she lowered her hands. The moment those words fell, the scene gradually quieted.

Soon after, an elderly villager spoke up. “Lord Angel, please return and rest at once. Leave the rest to us!”

“Lord Angel, thank you for your hard work!”

“Lord Angel, please take care of your health!”

“Lord Angel, I want to bear your children!”

“Lord Angel, savior of Aoma Village!”

“Lord Angel, have a safe journey!”

For a time, the villagers all spoke at once, and the scene descended into chaos. Fortunately, the disorder ended quickly. Yae-hime and her group carried the unconscious girl back to the village chief’s home.

“Everyone worked hard tonight. You should all go rest first. I still have some matters to attend to.” In the living room, Yae-hime glanced at the girl lying on the long bench and spoke.

The others obediently left the room, led by Angelica toward their resting quarters. Only Lili remained behind. She truly could not feel at ease about this girl.

“Lili, aren’t you going to rest?” Yae-hime looked over and asked.

“I’ll sleep with you,” Lili replied flatly. Yet inside, her heart pounded with tension.

Although the two of them had slept together before, that had been under special circumstances. Bringing it up on her own initiative now, she was genuinely afraid of being refused.

“That’s fine,” Yae-hime said with a smile. Since she still had to remain under watch anyway, sleeping together and chatting to pass the time sounded rather nice.

Hearing the reply, Lili immediately let out a breath of relief. The corners of her lips lifted slightly, sketching a faint, almost imperceptible smile.

“Sleeping will have to wait a bit. I’ll treat her first,” Yae-hime said.

“Mm, but I suggest you don’t fully heal her,” Lili nodded, then added with a serious expression.

“I was thinking the same.” Although she had not sensed any danger from this girl who was suspected to be of the Celestials, for safety’s sake, Yae-hime had no intention of healing her completely in one go.

Moreover, the mysterious lightning power contained within the girl’s body was not something she could absorb all at once. Recovering her in stages and over multiple sessions would allow the benefits to be maximized.

“Let’s observe first. If she turns out to be a threat to us, then…” As Lili spoke, a flash of icy killing intent flickered through her eyes.

“Relax. My intuition won’t be wrong,” Yae-hime said as she reached out and gently patted her head.

Lili’s expression instantly changed, so comfortable that she almost wanted to squint her eyes shut.

“Alright, it’s getting late. Let’s head back to the room,” Yae-hime said, withdrawing her hand and glancing at the unconscious girl.

At present, Angelica’s father had almost fully recovered and was in the living room. If he happened to see them treating the girl there, it would be difficult to explain.

Besides, she could not allow that pure, pristine body to be seen by some stinky man. That would be such a huge loss!

Lifting the girl suspected to be from the Celestials into her arms, Yae-hime stepped forward and headed for the guest room on the second floor.

Lili followed quickly behind. Before long, the two of them arrived inside the guest room. Yae-hime laid the girl on the bed and then deftly stripped her completely bare.

Seeing this, Lili froze for a moment before quickly regaining her composure. She knew this was Yae-hime’s usual habit when treating injuries. What she did not know was that only girls received this level of treatment. As for boys, a casual healing was more than enough. Why bother being so meticulous?

“This child seems to have quite a high-status background,” Lili said calmly as she looked at the clothes and exquisite accessories tossed to the side.

“You can tell,” Yae-hime nodded.

Even if the girl was not a Celestial, she was certainly a cultivator from a prominent family. Since ancient times, scholarship favored the poor, but martial paths favored the wealthy. And cultivation even more so.

Without money, dreaming of cultivation was nothing but folly.

“The burn marks on her body are still very fresh. She was probably struck by lightning within the last few days,” Yae-hime said softly as she carefully examined the body that looked as pristine as a newborn’s.

“Mm, those wounds show signs of recovery. This child’s self-healing ability is impressive,” Lili remarked. At the same time, her wariness toward the girl deepened.

“Her physique also seems exceptional,” Yae-hime said as her pupils abruptly turned emerald green, performing a precise internal scan of the girl.

Lili stood to the side without disturbing her. The room was so quiet that even a pin dropping could be heard.

Several minutes later, Yae-hime finished scanning, and her expression grew somewhat strange. ‘This child’s bodily structure… it feels like I’ve seen it somewhere before…’

“What’s wrong?” Seeing that expression, Lili could not help but ask.

“Her body structure is different from ordinary people’s. She doesn’t even have a heart!” Yae-hime said, turning her head with a tone of faint surprise.

“Huh?” Hearing that, several question marks practically popped up over Lili’s head.

+++

# **754 – Yae-hime’s Hypothesis and the Peculiar Bead**

Why was she still alive if she did not have a heart?

‘Could she be a demonic creature…?’ The thought surfaced, but Lili quickly shook her head and dismissed it.

“Although she doesn’t have a heart, she does have a substitute. A fist-sized energy crystal.” At that moment, Yae-hime recalled where she had seen a similar bodily structure before.

‘Her body shares some similarities with Vera’s clones!’

This girl, who was suspected to be of the Celestial race, turned out to be nothing more than a clone. The realization was simply unbelievable.

“An energy crystal… so she’s something like a clone?” Lili asked, confusion evident in her voice.

“Very likely.” Yae-hime nodded. This girl’s body indeed shared similarities with Vera’s clones. At the very least, the structural framework was alike. However, the internal composition of the girl’s body was far more intricate and complex.

“Gasp!” Upon hearing this, Lili involuntarily sucked in a sharp breath, her heart trembling with unease. The girl who made her feel such a strong sense of danger was merely a clone. Just how terrifying must the original body be?

At that moment, Lili erased the faint trace of killing intent from her heart. If she truly destroyed this clone, it would very likely invite serious trouble. It could even lead to a catastrophic disaster.

“Her original body is probably at least Legendary-tier, or even stronger…” Lili said softly, her small face turning pale.

“That strong?” Yae-hime asked in surprise.

Lili nodded lightly. “Yes. This clone is anything but ordinary. I can feel it. Her strength at her peak was absolutely terrifying.”

“Stronger than you?” Yae-hime found it hard to believe.

After hesitating for a moment, Lili still nodded. This time, it was Yae-hime who inhaled sharply. The temperature in the room seemed to rise noticeably. Because a mysterious force from the girl’s inner core was shielding her, Yae-hime had been unable to examine her clearly.

Now that Lili had said this, a very direct comparison finally took shape in her mind. This was an existence she could not afford to provoke.

“Then what should we do?” Yae-hime asked.

“How about quietly throwing her into the sea?” Lili suggested. After all, the girl had survived being swallowed by a sea beast. Drowning her was clearly impossible. If they were lucky, the ocean currents could carry her far away.

“Let’s not.” Yae-hime shook her head. She simply could not bring herself to do something so cruel. Even knowing the girl would not truly be in danger, it still felt wrong.

Besides, she and Lili had gone through so much effort to drive away the sea beast and obtain this ‘spoils of war.’ There was no way she could just throw it away.

“But keeping her here is still a hidden risk,” Lili said. Although she did not fully understand clones, she knew they shared certain special connections with their original bodies.

The stronger the clone, the stronger that connection tended to be. Because of that, killing her outright was out of the question. And secretly discarding her was something little Hime clearly refused to do.

Lili bit her cherry-red lips, thinking it over again and again, yet unable to come up with a proper solution.

“I’ve decided,” Yae-hime suddenly said.

“Decided what?” Lili looked at her, puzzled.

“Let’s wake her up first,” Yae-hime replied.

“We don’t even know if she’s an enemy or an ally. Waking her so easily feels risky,” Lili said with concern.

“It’s fine. I don’t sense any danger,” Yae-hime said calmly.

From the girl, she only felt a subtle sense of familiarity. ‘Could it be that this child really is of the Celestial race?’

At that moment, doubt quietly rose in her heart.

In the end, Yae-hime only knew the period when the Celestial race appeared on a large scale. She had no idea whether Celestials had existed even earlier than that. If what Lili said was correct, this girl possessed at least Legendary-level strength.

On the Southern Continent, among the factions Yae-hime knew, anyone at the Legendary tier was a dominant figure in their own right. And a single clone already counted as such a figure. That meant the girl’s true body was, at the very least, of Mythical level.

As for anything beyond that, Yae-hime did not even dare to imagine it. No matter how one looked at it, this girl could not possibly be some ordinary cultivator.

‘She’s one hundred percent a Celestial, and within her race, she definitely held no small status!’ Suddenly, a flash of insight streaked through her mind. ‘Right, my bloodline quest still hasn’t been activated. A Celestial appearing at a time like this… it does seem to fit.’

At that thought, Yae-hime merely smiled faintly. To her, the cost-performance of bloodline quests was far too low, practically a tasteless burden.

Asking her to travel thousands of kilometers to the Celestial Island just to activate such a quest was honestly more trouble than it was worth.

She lacked neither resources nor guidance from capable mentors. Going there might even result in her freedom being restricted, just like Nangong Lin and the others.

‘If the bloodline quest were carried out within the Jade Empire, that would be another matter.’

Her foundation was right here. As long as the rebellion succeeded, the benefits she would reap would be endless. There was absolutely no need to endure countless hardships to reach the Celestial Island.

“Little Hime?” Seeing her spacing out, Lili stepped closer, waving a small hand in front of her face.

“Sorry, I got a bit distracted,” Yae-hime said as she came back to herself, sounding slightly embarrassed.

“So you really plan to wake her up?” Lili withdrew her gaze from Yae-hime and looked toward the unconscious girl lying on the bed.

“Yes. It’s necessary,” Yae-hime replied as she walked forward, her pupils abruptly turning jade-green. Whether or not the girl was a key figure for triggering a quest, she intended to wake her up.

“Alright, but don’t restore too much,” Lili said helplessly as she saw the seriousness in her expression and nodded. After all, matters involving the Child of Destiny were not something she could interfere with excessively.

‘I need to stay fully alert in case anything happens!’ Lili stared intently at the girl on the bed, thinking to herself. At present, this was all she could do.

Yae-hime wasted no more words. A green needle condensed in her hand and swiftly pierced into the girl’s unguarded chest.

“Mmm…” As if sensing a faint pain, the girl let out a soft moan, yet she did not wake up.

Yae-hime paid it no mind. The green needle in her hand stabbed again and again, fast as lightning. In the next instant, several surges of powerful life energy flooded into the girl’s body.

Watching the burn marks on the girl’s skin fade away at an astonishing speed, Lili still felt a sense of awe in her heart. ‘Little Hime’s medical skill is truly miraculous!’

After all, those were no ordinary burns, but lingering injuries caused by lightning infused with profound laws!

Yae-hime drove the final needle into the girl’s lower abdomen. Her gaze sharpened as she plunged the entire green needle in. She then pressed her palm lightly against the spot, simultaneously pouring in her own life energy while drawing out the lightning power within the girl’s body.

The sensation she had experienced on the deserted island surged through her once more. Crackling and tingling, numb yet electrifying, it was almost blissful.

Fortunately, thanks to her previous experience, Yae-hime had built up some resistance and was not sent reeling by the impact. This time, she continuously observed her own body from within.

Sure enough, she saw the lightning energy rapidly flow toward the rotating golden bead, where it was completely absorbed, causing the bead to emit a faint glow. An extremely profound aura spread out along with it.

‘This bead seems to grow stronger after absorbing lightning power. Wait. If it can absorb lightning, does that mean it can absorb other types of power as well?’ Moved by the thought, Yae-hime immediately acted, attaching a trace of life energy to the bead.

In the blink of an eye, it was absorbed completely.

+++

# **755 – This One Is a Threat!**

Seeing this entirely expected change, Yae-hime’s expression remained calm, yet inside she was practically bursting with excitement.

‘Wonderful, simply wonderful!’ This golden bead could absorb life energy, which meant it could store life energy. It could even store other forms of energy as well. ‘Even though I don’t yet know how to use this little bead, the fact that it can store power alone already makes it incredible!’

In the game, Yae-hime never had to worry about running out of energy. Out in the real world, however, things were completely different. She had no items that could rapidly replenish her mana.

Relying solely on passive energy absorption was far from sufficient. If she ever ran into a dangerous situation, that shortfall could be fatal. Now that she could store energy inside the golden bead and take it with her, it was essentially the same as obtaining a recovery item.

As for how effective it was, she had not tested it yet, so she did not know. She also had not figured out how to properly use it. Still, anything obtained for free was always a delight.

“Mmmn…”

Just as Yae-hime was about to study the golden bead more closely, the young girl suddenly let out a lazy, muffled groan.

Her eyelashes trembled, and she slowly opened her eyes. They were pitch-black eyes, deep like an abyssal pool, exuding an indescribable allure.

The moment she saw this, Lili’s entire body tensed. Her small hands clenched tightly as energy surged within her, ready to erupt at any moment.

“You’re awake,” Yae-hime said calmly, her tone casual and unhurried. She had only restored the girl’s bodily functions. Not a trace of her strength had returned. In other words, the girl was harmless in her current state.

Still groggy from just waking up, the girl heard the voice and instinctively looked over. The fog in her mind cleared the instant her gaze fell on Yae-hime, and her thoughts began to move again.

She stared at Yae-hime without saying a word.

“Do you feel unwell anywhere?” Yae-hime asked.

“…” The girl did not respond. She blinked, her expression full of confusion. ‘Who am I? Where am I? And who is this pretty older sister in front of me?’

As those thoughts formed, a dull ache spread through her head. Fragments of scattered memories surged chaotically, as though they were about to tear her mind apart and burst free.

“Do you feel unwell anywhere?” Seeing her suddenly clutch her head with both hands, her face contorting in pain, Yae-hime asked again. This time, concern was evident in her voice.

Lili grew even more vigilant, her beautiful eyes never leaving the girl for even half a second.

“*￥%…&%…” The girl’s headache intensified to the point of agony, and she began muttering meaningless sounds.

‘It looks like her brain has suffered serious damage.’ Yae-hime’s eyes instantly turned emerald-green as she once again saw through the girl’s body, immediately pinpointing the problem.

Traces of lightning energy were raging violently within the girl’s brain.

‘This wasn’t present while she was unconscious. It must have appeared after she woke up.’ With that thought, Yae-hime condensed a thin green needle and, in a flash, pierced it into the girl’s head.

She immediately extracted the lightning energy from within. The entire process was incredibly swift. By the time the girl could even react, it was already over.

“All done. You’re fine now,” Yae-hime said as she withdrew her hand, a gentle smile spreading across her face.

The girl continued holding her head, her small face filled with confusion. Then, as realization dawned on her, she looked up at Yae-hime. ‘She helped me? That’s strange… this person makes me feel very comfortable, very close.’

“Do you feel unwell anywhere else?” Yae-hime asked softly.

The girl shook her head.

‘That’s odd. I clearly couldn’t understand what she was saying before, yet now I can…’ No matter how much she thought about it, she could not make sense of it.

“That’s good to hear. By the way, what’s your name?” Yae-hime bent down slightly and asked in a friendly tone. She felt there was something off about this girl, as if she was not quite all there mentally.

“Na… name…” The girl’s delicate brows knitted together as she tried hard to recall it. Her mind was filled only with scattered fragments, and very little usable information. After searching for a while, she finally remembered her name.

“Zerene.”

Aside from her name, everything else remained a blank. It felt as though, unless those fragments were pieced back together, she would never be able to recover her memories.

“Zerene, that’s a lovely name,” Yae-hime said with a smile. She then asked, “Where are you from?”

Hearing this, the girl who called herself Zerene tried hard to recall it again. Yet the only thing that surfaced in her mind was terrifying heavenly lightning. Bolts of thunder had rained down upon her again and again, like divine punishment, relentlessly tormenting her.

“No!” As the memory surfaced, Zerene clutched her head with both hands, her entire body trembling uncontrollably. It was clear that she was genuinely terrified.

Such a reaction left both Yae-hime and Lili utterly confused.

“She looks… kind of strange,” Lili said in a low voice.

“Yes, something’s wrong with her mind,” Yae-hime nodded lightly.

“Her mind is broken?” Lili asked in mild surprise.

“It seems like amnesia,” Yae-hime replied.

All the symptoms Zerene displayed were consistent with memory loss. Combined with what she had just seen through her earlier inspection, it was essentially confirmed.

“So her brain was probably damaged by the heavenly lightning,” Lili said, instantly relaxing. Severely injured and having lost her memories, this version of Zerene posed little threat to them.

“Don’t worry. No one here will hurt you,” Yae-hime said softly as she looked at Zerene.

For some reason, upon hearing that voice, the fear in Zerene’s heart suddenly diminished by a great deal. She lifted her head and looked at Yae-hime, the sense of closeness growing ever stronger. It was as if she were looking at a family member.

“I remember something scary… but I can’t remember anything else,” Zerene said pitifully, tears welling up in her eyes.

Even so, Lili remained somewhat on guard. Until she was certain the other party was harmless, she could not completely relax.

“It’s alright. I’m here. Nothing will happen to you,” Yae-hime said, reaching out to gently pat Zerene’s head.

Zerene blinked her watery eyes, suddenly feeling an overwhelming urge to cry. She desperately wanted to cling to the stunningly beautiful girl in front of her and burst into sobs.

No, she already had. She threw herself into Yae-hime’s arms and cried without restraint.

Lili tried to pull Zerene away from Yae-hime, but the latter stopped her.

“She’s very unsettled,” Yae-hime said softly. As she spoke, she gently stroked Zerene’s back.

Watching this scene, Lili felt a sour sensation rise in her chest, leaving her deeply uncomfortable. ‘This Zerene is a major threat!’

Crying and crying, Zerene eventually fell asleep.

“She’s just like a little child,” Lili said unhappily.

‘You’ve cried before too.’ Yae-hime rolled her eyes.

After placing Zerene onto the bed, the two of them stood off to the side.

“Do you think she could be acting?” Lili asked quietly.

“No. I know her physical condition very well,” Yae-hime shook her head.

“I see,” Lili said softly as she looked at the sleeping Zerene.

Compared to before, her sleeping face was noticeably more peaceful.

“At this point, we don’t even know if she’s an enemy or an ally. That’s troublesome.” Lili withdrew her gaze and let out a quiet sigh. If Zerene had shown hostility or goodwill the moment she woke up, things would have been easier to deal with.

But now she had amnesia. No one knew whether she would regain her memories. And if she did, whether she would become an enemy.

“Let’s wait and see,” Yae-hime said optimistically. She was still inclined to trust her own instincts. “Enough of that. It’s getting late. Let’s rest.”

As she spoke, Yae-hime lay down on her side on the bed, her pale hand lightly patting the mattress as she beckoned Lili over.

“All three of us sleeping on such a small bed?” Lili said indignantly, glancing at the sound-asleep Zerene.

+++

# **756 – That’s It? Seriously?**

“Can’t be helped. There’s only one guest room here,” Yae-hime said evenly. She did not seem to think that the three of them sleeping together was anything strange. She was not the kind of person who slept around casually.

Sleeping beside an unfamiliar girl would normally make her feel somewhat uncomfortable. Yet Zerene gave her no such feeling at all. On the contrary, there was an inexplicable sense of closeness.

“But I don’t want to sleep with her,” Lili said, folding her arms across her chest as she puffed out her lips.

“Just pretend Zerene is invisible,” Yae-hime replied as she patted the mattress again. “See? If I sleep on my side like this, you won’t even see her.”

“….” Hearing that, Lili blinked, struggled inwardly for a moment, and finally gave in. “Fine. But only this once,” she said, lowering her arms and shooting Yae-hime an aggrieved look.

The latter smiled and beckoned to her.

“Hmph.” Lili snorted, then stepped forward. With a soft swish, she kicked off her boots and slipped straight into Yae-hime’s embrace. “Like this, I won’t see that girl at all,” she murmured, burying her head into the other’s chest.

“It’s late. Let’s sleep,” Yae-hime said, reaching out to switch off the magic crystal lamp before resting her hand on Lili.

“Mm,” Lili replied softly, her small face tinged with red.

Her heart began to pound even faster. Sleeping while hugging each other this closely really was bad for her heart.

Lili closed her eyes and muttered to herself inwardly.

The room fell quiet. Yae-hime, however, remained awake. She had originally planned to chat with Lili, or perhaps do a full-body beauty routine to pass the time. But when she thought about what Lili had done today, she changed her mind.

“You’ve really worked hard today,” Yae-hime said softly.

Lili did not respond. Only faint breathing sounds echoed through the room.

Zerene’s, and Lili’s.

Clearly, Lili had already drifted into sleep. It was obvious that she was utterly exhausted today.

‘The apostle didn’t come, but instead a sea beast appeared, and that sea beast ended up bringing me a Celestial. Today was full of surprises.’ Thinking back on everything that had happened, Yae-hime could not help but sigh inwardly.

There was no need for her to worry about Alicia for now. As for the apostle threat facing Aoma Village, with Lili around, it was not much of a problem either.

‘As for Zerene, I still don’t know what’s going on. I’ll just observe for now.’

Feeling the faint warmth coming from her back, Yae-hime frowned slightly. Even though the Celestial race girl did not give her any sense of danger or crisis… She still felt that the timing of her appearance was far too coincidental. As if the two of them were fated to meet.

‘Fate, huh… Alicia seems to believe in things like fate.’

Whether Yae-hime believed in it or not, the answer was naturally yes. After all, she herself was someone who had been reborn.

‘It feels like we’re all chess pieces, moving around on the board under the arrangements of some god of fate.’

Yae-hime had entertained a few conjectures about her own rebirth. But those guesses were so absurd that even she found them hard to believe. Unless there was concrete evidence to support them…

The night grew deeper.

Yae-hime’s “penalty time” finally came to an end.

She glanced at Lili in her arms and whispered softly, “We’ll see each other again tomorrow morning.”

As soon as the words fell, Yae-hime logged out at once. Zerene and Lili continued sleeping, as if they were completely unaware of the changes outside.

---

At this moment, atop the City of Chaos.

Yae-hime opened her eyes and slowly let out a breath of stale air. “So tired. Today was really rough.” She got up from the bed and stretched lazily.

“Master!” A small figure suddenly flashed into view, a lively voice spreading through the room.

Looking up, she saw Little Blue swooping toward her.

“Good evening!” Little Blue said cheerfully as she leapt straight into Yae-hime’s arms, wrapping her arms around her neck and rubbing her cheek against her.

“You look so happy. Did something good happen?” Yae-hime pinched her soft, rosy cheek and asked with a smile.

“Mm-hmm! Chef One got upgraded. Everything it cooks now tastes better and better!” Little Blue said happily.

“That really is good news.” Yae-hime nodded lightly. “As long as you all behave yourselves, there’ll definitely be no shortage of premium ingredients.”

“Yay! I knew Master was the best!” Little Blue exclaimed excitedly.

That was exactly why she had rushed out so eagerly. She wanted Yae-hime to buy some high-grade ingredients so Chef One could cook something delicious.

“You think I don’t know what you’re plotting?” Yae-hime said as she gently lifted Little Blue off her. Then she asked, “Has anything changed on Aqua Blue Star?”

Little Blue floated in midair, her face full of smiles. “Master, everything’s normal!”

“No news is good news.” Yae-hime let out a breath of relief. With trouble constantly brewing in the game, if the real world also spiraled into chaos, it would definitely give her a splitting headache.

“Did anyone special arrive in Cathay today?” Yae-hime asked casually as she stood up.

By now, the news that S.K.Y. possessed an artifact had already spread across the world. She felt that some major overseas powers would likely make a move.

As for the local powerhouses, Mylene had not received any particular updates. Those people seemed to be waiting and watching.

What Yae-hime did not know was that the major domestic powers currently had no time to worry about S.K.Y. at all. Most of them were busy figuring out how to make contact with the so-called Kun Ruins prodigy.

And who else could that prodigy be, if not Yae-hime herself?

Unfortunately, Yae-hime was not from Kun Ruins at all. She did not even know where Kun Ruins was. So whatever plans they were making around her, hoping to gain some benefit, were nothing more than wishful thinking.

“Yes. Quite a few transcendent and martial artists arrived throughout the day,” Little Blue reported.

“Many S-rankers or Grandmasters?” Yae-hime asked.

Little Blue shook her head. “Nope. Just a bunch of small fries.”

“Looks like the big overseas powers aren’t planning to make their move yet. Keep an eye on things for me.” Yae-hime instructed.

“Okay! Oh right, Master. Chef One made a late-night snack. Do you want to eat together?” Little Blue nodded, suddenly remembering the food.

Yae-hime shook her head lightly. “I’m not hungry. You all go ahead.”

“Alright then, I’ll eat it while it’s hot!” With that, Little Blue flashed away, vanishing in an instant.

“She sure runs fast… that little glutton.” Yae-hime said with a wry smile. After that, she closed her eyes and turned her attention inward, examining the changes within her body.

‘The bead really is still there!’ The moment she saw the golden bead, the corners of her lips lifted slightly, forming a pleased smile.

“Great. This gives me double… no, triple insurance!” Yae-hime said excitedly.

As Aqua Blue Star awakened, the dangers she faced in the real world were very likely to surpass those in the game. Having another life-saving trump card was naturally a good thing.

“The problem now is that I don’t know how to use it… Forget it. I’ll just figure it out as I go!” Once the thought crossed her mind, Yae-hime immediately put it into action and tried to draw upon the bead’s power.

The result came effortlessly.

The moment she tried to pull out a trace of life energy, the bead responded on its own, releasing it naturally. Being able to control the bead’s power so easily actually left Yae-hime feeling a little unaccustomed. She froze for several seconds before finally reacting.

“It worked? That’s it? It really worked just like that?” As she spoke, her expression gradually turned into uncontrollable joy.

+++

# **757 – Live On With Dignity**

“Heh, this is truly excellent!” Lightly clenching her fist, Yae-hime smiled so brightly that her face seemed to bloom like peach blossoms.

She had thought it would take some time to study the bead before she could use it, yet it turned out to be effortlessly mastered, as natural as moving a part of her own body.

No, that was not quite right. It really was a part of Yae-hime’s body. After all, it had been born from within her.

“Since it’s a part of me, using it should naturally be as easy as flipping my palm.” As she spoke, Yae-hime actually loosened her grip and flipped her hand over. Now, she officially possessed a third trump card, and her confidence surged.

“I wonder how much energy it can store?” Her intuition told her that the bead’s capacity was absolutely terrifying. After all, this bead could even absorb lightning energy imbued with profound and mysterious laws.

“Let’s test it.” A woman of action, Yae-hime moved decisively, acting the moment the thought crossed her mind.

In the next instant, a considerable amount of life energy within her body surged toward the rotating golden bead. Very quickly, all of that life energy was swallowed up by the golden bead.

Yae-hime continued feeding it. The golden bead kept devouring everything greedily, as though it had no concept of fullness at all.

Ten minutes later, her face turned slightly pale as she stopped, her cherry lips parting. “This is a bottomless pit!”

Even as she felt astonished, a wave of delight rose in her heart. Because the harder this bead was to fill, the more useful it would be to her. Who would ever complain about having a warehouse that was too big?

Next, Yae-hime tried extracting the energy stored inside and discovered that the speed was somewhat slower than absorption. This meant that rapidly drawing energy during combat to replenish herself would be somewhat difficult.

“That doesn’t really count as a flaw.” Compared to its advantages, this shortcoming was completely negligible. So Yae-hime did not pay it much mind.

Moreover, after absorbing such massive amounts of lightning energy, the bead might undergo some kind of mutation. When that happened, this minor flaw might very well disappear entirely.

After extracting all the life energy from the bead, her complexion immediately improved. At the same time, the changes in her body became especially apparent.

“I’m much stronger than before.” Feeling the power constantly surging within her, Yae-hime remained calm and composed.

In the game, she had reached level 40. Upon returning to the real world, a boost in strength was only natural. It was nothing worth making a fuss over.

“With my current strength, I should be at the peak Grandmaster level, only one step away from Great Perfection. In all of Cathay, I’m afraid only Lisa is slightly stronger than me.”

After a Grandmaster passes through the five minor stages of Primary, Intermediate, Advanced, Pinnacle, and Great Perfection, they can step into an even higher major realm.

However, due to the depletion of spiritual energy, no one had yet entered the legendary Martial Saint realm.

“Mylene told me that Lisa already has half a foot in that realm. To reach that level in an era of depleted spiritual energy is truly astonishing.”

Only after reaching the pinnacle stage did Yae-hime truly understand just how formidable Lisa was.

“If we only compare basic strength, I’m not her opponent for now. But if we use skills and trump cards, we’d be evenly matched, or I might even gain a slight edge.” Clenching her fist again, Yae-hime murmured to herself.

Through her duel with Lucky, she had seen her own shortcomings. That was her crude martial techniques. When she could not use skills, she relied purely on overwhelming strength to crush her opponent, which made those flaws invisible.

“If skills are forbidden and our strength is equal, I’d suffer quite a bit at Lucky’s hands. Against someone on Lisa’s level, it would be even worse.” Those masters who were proficient in traditional martial arts were all far from simple!

“Come to think of it, traditional martial arts were originally practical killing techniques that evolved with the times. They’re completely different from the modern routine-style gymnastics. Unfortunately, times had changed.” Yae-hime let out a soft sigh.

This era had little need for traditional martial arts, and coupled with various restrictions, they could no longer truly flourish on this land. Only a small number of people were still preserving the tradition.

“Even if I want to learn…” At that point, Yae-hime suddenly thought of someone. She immediately picked up her phone and sent a message.

Before long, a reply came back.

Mylene: Sister, you want a large number of traditional martial arts videos. Are you trying to study some kind of ultimate killing move?

Yae-hime: More or less. Do you have any on hand? I’m not looking for videos of ordinary martial arts masters.

Mylene: I do! And they’re all Grandmaster-level ones! Sister, wait a moment!

“Sure enough, my little sister is the most reliable.” Sitting down on the bed, Yae-hime spoke with heartfelt satisfaction.

Her request for Grandmaster-level traditional martial arts videos was primarily to study the techniques within.

As for the application of qi, she had not the slightest interest. Because when it came to the use of qi, she was absolutely at the pinnacle of this world.

Before long, Mylene sent over a total of 150 GB of video files.

“Good thing this phone is using the Nangong family’s network. Otherwise, once the 50 GB limit ran out, the speed would’ve been throttled.”

Seeing the videos transferring at a steady speed of eight megabytes per second, Yae-hime nodded in satisfaction. She then returned to the phone’s home screen, opened the trending news section, and browsed the latest hot topics.

The first thing that caught her eye was the number one trending search.

“I’m Injured,” by Ryan.

Opening it up, she saw that the popular young male celebrity Ryan had injured his pinky finger while filming a drama. The wound was actually a full one millimeter long!

The comments below were filled with people expressing heartache for Ryan, calling him “husband” over and over again, making Yae-hime’s scalp tingle.

“One millimeter long. What an exaggerated injury. It would probably heal on its own before he even reached the hospital.” She closed the first trending topic and muttered to herself.

Then she looked at the second trending search.

“The artifact’s owner turns out to be the former top MOBA game KOK’s War God, S.K.Y.!”

“No shock at all. Good review.” Yae-hime nodded and moved on to the third trending topic. Even without opening it, she knew there would be no important information about S.K.Y. inside. There was no need to waste time.

“Oh? My topic actually made it to third place.” She said this with mild surprise.

It was common knowledge that trending searches could be bought with money. To reach the top three without spending a cent spoke volumes about the level of attention it had drawn.

“It’s probably people smearing me again.” Seeing the title «The Black-Hearted Princess Is Truly Terrifying!», Yae-hime could not even be bothered to click into it.

Letting out a soft breath, she switched apps and looked at the file transfer software. It showed that all videos had finished downloading.

“It’s time to absorb some new nourishment.” Holding her phone, Yae-hime left the room and headed to an open area outside the city. “Fifteen Grandmasters, fifteen inheritance recordings. It’s a pity I don’t have time to study them all.”

Looking at the names of the martial arts displayed on the phone screen, Yae-hime found herself momentarily unsure of what to choose. She naturally understood the principle that biting off more than one could chew would only backfire.

After ten minutes of deliberation, she chose three styles: Bagua Palm, Bajiquan, Taiji

“Bagua Palm has agile footwork, making it suitable for prolonged engagements. Bajiquan is fierce and explosive, making it excellent as a finishing technique. Taiji balances hardness and softness, fast and slow, and has extremely strong practicality.”

Based on her own traits, Yae-hime decided to practice these three disciplines. Among them, Taiji was divided into Wudang Sanfeng-style, Chen-style, and Li-style.

The most orthodox was undoubtedly Wudang Sanfeng-style, which consisted of twelve core forms. Chen-style and Li-style Taiji were both derived from Wudang Taiji, with many techniques and formidable real combat effectiveness.

“Once I master Wudang Taiji, learning Chen-style and Li-style Taiji will be much easier.” With that, Yae-hime officially began her video-based study.

+++

# **758: Arrangements in the City of Chaos**

An hour later.

“So that’s how it is. Taiji with qi and Taiji without qi aren’t even the same martial art.” After watching the Taiji Grandmaster’s inheritance video, Yae-hime immediately gained a much deeper understanding of traditional martial arts.

Qi was the true foundation of everything. The outward postures existed only to better channel and release qi. When strength and qi were fused together, they could unleash terrifying power.

“The so-called ‘four ounces to deflect a thousand pounds’ is nothing but an embellished myth. If a force truly weighing a thousand pounds came crashing down… and you didn’t possess enough strength to neutralize it, you would be crushed to death without question.”

She bent down, placed her phone on the floor, and smiled wryly as she spoke. After all, without sufficient strength, one could not even achieve true neutralization of force.

Taiji’s softness was, in truth, built upon a foundation of hardness. Using softness to overcome hardness was merely one way of borrowing strength. One had to ask, how could a weak person possibly use techniques alone to borrow a strong opponent’s power and strike back? That was simply impossible.

As the saying went, sheer strength could suppress all techniques. No matter how many tricks one had, overwhelming power could smash straight through them.

“Taiji places extremely high demands on physical conditioning… it’s a bit different from what I imagined. But thinking about it, that makes sense. This martial art was created by Daoist Sanfeng, a figure revered as both a Martial Saint and an Earthly Immortal. The power of the techniques that survived to this day probably isn’t even one percent of what they were back then. In fact, it’s questionable whether these techniques retained even a trace of their original spirit.”

Yae-hime muttered to herself. Then her arms lowered naturally before slowly rising again. Her movements were gentle, yet they carried an inexplicable sense of force. It felt as though a single palm strike could fell an entire crowd.

From slow to fast, then from fast back to slow, she spent over a minute completing the twelve forms.

“Hah… that was a bit tiring.” She exhaled softly as her hands slowly drew back in.

After finishing this Sanfeng-style Taiji set, she had already mastered the use of qi. Such talent was astonishingly brilliant… no, terrifyingly so. If the Taiji Grandmaster who left behind that inheritance recording were to see this, he would probably kneel on the spot.

Immediately after, Yae-hime went on to learn Chen-style and Li-style Taiji as well, integrating and refining them into a Taiji of her own.

“My talent is kind of ridiculous.” Feeling the flow of qi circulating through her body, Yae-hime murmured to herself. The bloodlines and various attribute points she had gained in the game were now revealing their true value in reality.

Her powerful Talent granted her an unparalleled capacity for comprehension. The bonuses from her various attributes meant that no matter what martial art she learned, she achieved twice the result with half the effort.

“A once-in-a-millennium martial arts prodigy is probably about my level.” She said it calmly, without the slightest ripple of emotion in her heart. After all, her talent had manifested itself far more vividly in the game.

With time still to spare, Yae-hime pressed on without pause, practicing Bajiquan and Bagua Palm. Thanks to her foundation in Taiji, learning these two martial arts was light and effortless.

Before long, she completed her training. Then came repeated practice and refinement to become familiar with them.

Not far away, Little Blue and the five Vera clones stood in place, staring unblinkingly as Yae-hime practiced her forms.

“Master is really amazing,” Vera 18 sighed. She knew very well that her master had not known these techniques prior to this.

“Mm. She’s becoming more and more unfathomable,” Vera 17 nodded. ‘Her talent is so great she scarcely seemed human.’

“Her techniques are becoming increasingly refined. She’s optimizing them!” Vera 1 exclaimed in astonishment. As the earliest clone of Vera, she was naturally well-informed and had some understanding of martial arts.

What Yae-hime was doing now was what one would call refinement. This was something only those extremely familiar with the techniques and possessed of the appropriate talent could accomplish. Yet now, this breathtaking existence was doing it with ease. How could that not shock her?

“A genius… no, this is a monster…” Even Vera 3’s usually indifferent face was filled with shock.

“So this is our master? She’s incredible!” Vera 2 said excitedly, little stars sparkling in her eyes.

“Hehe, of course Master is amazing!” Little Blue floated in midair with her hands on her hips, boasting proudly.

As if hearing their voices, Yae-hime drew her hands back and slowly lowered them, bringing today’s training to an end. In just a little over two hours, she had gained insights that would take other grandmasters an entire lifetime to comprehend. It was a truly bountiful harvest.

“Are you all done eating?” Yae-hime asked as she looked at them.

“Mhm! I’m totally stuffed!” Little Blue replied, streaking over like a bolt of lightning.

The Vera clones hurried forward to follow.

“Look at you. You eat and don’t even wipe your mouth afterward. All greasy and oily.” Catching Little Blue as she flew over, clearly intending to cling to her and rub all over her, Yae-hime scolded her with exasperation.

She then released a trace of qi, neatly cleaning Little Blue’s small mouth.

“Hehe, Master, how did your training go?” The little one laughed carefree and unbothered.

“It was decent.” Yae-hime pinched her tiny nose. “I picked up three pretty good martial arts.”

Hearing this, the Vera clones who had just caught up were all stunned. They had assumed Yae-hime had only learned a single set.

By all logic, mastering even one respectable martial art in such a short time already meant one possessed heaven-defying talent. Using the same amount of time to master three solid martial arts… such an existence would be called a monster.

Before their eyes, this peerlessly beautiful being was precisely that, a thoroughly terrifying monster.

“Master, you’re amazing… ah, I can’t even find the right words. Anyway, totally invincible. Absolutely cracked!” Vera 18 said excitedly.

“Mhm, invincible!” Vera 17 echoed.

Vera 1, 2, and 3 also nodded, their expressions a mix of astonishment and disbelief.

“It’s nothing special.” Yae-hime replied calmly. To her, this was merely normal procedure. It was not something worth boasting about or taking pride in.

“Master is the best!” At that moment, Little Blue wrapped her arms around Yae-hime’s neck and rubbed her cheek against her energetically.

“Alright, stop fooling around.” Yae-hime lifted her off. “I have something serious to discuss with you.”

Hearing this, Little Blue immediately restrained herself, her expression turning solemn. The Vera clones promptly closed their mouths, waiting for Yae-hime to speak. The scene fell quiet, with only the faint sound of the breeze lingering in the air.

“It won’t be long before we return the City of Chaos over there.” Yae-hime went straight to the point. Now that the five Vera sisters were already on her side, there was no harm in letting them know such information.

“Ohhh, so we’re finally about to do something big!” Little Blue floated in midair, clenching her pink fists excitedly.

“That’s right. Before that, we need to repair the City of Chaos. The materials are almost all collected. Once we return to the Saint Demon World, we can immediately begin the repairs. As for where we’ll return to, I’ve already found a suitable location.” Yae-hime said.

“Yay, yay! I finally get a chance to really show what I can do!” Little Blue danced around happily, brimming with excitement.

The five Vera sisters listened to their exchange, their expressions shifting in all sorts of ways. Even though they had long known that Yae-hime and Little Blue were anything but ordinary, they were still deeply shaken by the two of them once again.

+++

# **759 – If It Were You…**

“Little Blue, roughly how long will it take to repair City of Chaos?” Yae-hime brushed aside her black hair that had been tousled by the wind and asked.

Based on her estimation, Alicia would need around four to five days to recover her strength to its peak. The restoration of City of Chaos had to be completed before that.

Little Blue pondered for a moment, then replied, “About a day and a half to two days.”

“Mm. Then two days from now, we’ll return to the Saint Demon World. By the way, the unfinished building has already been renovated, right?” Yae-hime asked.

“It’s been done ages ago. There’s a bathroom, a kitchen, and a big bed, super comfortable. And when the time comes, I’ll even leave Chef One behind to cook for them!” Little Blue said proudly, hands on her hips.

“Good.” Yae-hime patted her on the head, then turned her gaze toward the five Vera sisters. “While we’re away, you’ll stay on standby in the unfinished building.”

“Yes!” The five of them nodded in unison.

Before Yae-hime had woken up, they had already seen the accommodations there. Although it could not compare to the rooms in City of Chaos, the difference was not that great.

More importantly, during the few days they stayed there, they would be able to eat plenty of meals made with high-grade ingredients. No loss at all.

After chatting casually with everyone for a while, Yae-hime returned to her room and lay down on the bed to rest.

“Things left behind by the ancestors still have plenty worth learning from.” She stared at the ceiling, slowly raised her hand, then suddenly snapped her arm forward. The surrounding space rippled faintly as if shaken, and a sharp boom echoed through the room.

“Grandmaster-level martial techniques really are exquisite. When it comes to utilizing the body, they were undeniably far superior to me. Of course, that was before.”

Now that she had formally trained in grandmaster-level martial techniques, she had surpassed her predecessors entirely. Even if those three grandmasters were called over to fight her head-on, Yae-hime could still use the same techniques to knock them flat.

“Now I have martial techniques, basic skills, and sword manipulation. As long as I don’t run into a Martial Saint–level monster, I can still fight.”

After the previous round of training, Yae-hime’s strength had climbed another small step. Even if she ran into Lisa, there was nothing to worry about. As for the so-called Martial Saints or overseas Sages, whether they even existed was still an open question.

“Those ancient creatures are known dangers. Fortunately, they’re still in the process of awakening.” Retracting her hand, Yae-hime stared at the ceiling and murmured to herself.

Aside from the monster in the southern Pacific waters, she had yet to see similar existences appear elsewhere. Moreover, after showing itself once, that creature had vanished without a trace.

Little Blue and Yae-hime suspected that it had only awakened temporarily and had not truly revived. After all, the planet’s recovery had only just begun, and there simply was not enough ambient energy for it to absorb.

“After sleeping for hundreds, even thousands of years, their bodies must be starving, desperate to recover.”

As long as those ancient beings could not return to their full strength in a short time, they posed little threat to her.

What’s more, once part of the City of Chaos’ functions had been restored, it would undoubtedly give her wings like a tiger, allowing her to sweep across everything in her path.

There was truly nothing to worry about.

“Only by being strong oneself can one remain at ease in any situation.” Yae-hime closed her eyes and said softly. As her words fell, the room gradually grew quiet.

---

Inside the game, within the Celestial Island palace.

“Judging by the timing, Zerene should have already arrived on the Southern Continent by now. I wonder if she’s met the Child of Destiny?”

Seated upon an exquisitely carved jade throne was a young girl as delicate as sculpted jade, her bearing noble and refined. Her voice echoed through the grand hall, yet no one answered.

“Unfortunately, I am bound by the Heavenly Law and cannot observe what’s happening over there.” The powerful Celestial being let out a soft sigh, then gently swung her beautiful, jade-like feet.

For some reason, an inexplicable sense of unease had lingered in her heart lately. Clearly, her external incarnation possessed considerable strength, so there should have been no need for concern.

“I hope nothing goes wrong.” Looking toward the outside of the grand hall, she murmured quietly.

At this moment, in the guest room of the village chief’s house in Aoma Village, the girl who called herself Zerene was still sleeping soundly. Beside her, Lili slept just as peacefully.

Under the same sky, within the church of Jade City. At this time, those foreign clerics had already been arranged accommodations at nearby inns.

The bishop and Passat were arranged to stay in the church’s high-grade VIP suites.

“Passat, I heard you were beaten up?” In the living room, Bishop Gurant sat on a plush sofa, lightly sipping a glass of crimson fruit wine as he looked at the young man seated opposite him and asked.

“Yes, Your Grace,” Passat replied, leaning back against the sofa with one leg crossed over the other, his tone casual and unconcerned.

“You didn’t retaliate. That surprises me,” Gurant said.

Although the two were, in name, in a superior–subordinate relationship, Passat was, after all, a member of the Golden Aslan family, so he was naturally treated differently from an ordinary subordinate.

“Your Grace, that’s because I’ve fallen in love,” Passat said with a smile. That smile was thick with an oily, cloying quality.

“May the Goddess bless you,” Gurant replied flatly. There was not the slightest hint of sincerity in those words. Even so, Passat was clearly delighted.

“Your Grace, I have an impertinent request.”

“Oh? Let’s hear it,” Gurant said as he set down his wineglass and fixed his gaze on Passat.

“I hope you can strip this church’s Saintess, Irene, of her saintly status. As for the price, I guarantee it will satisfy you!” Passat said excitedly. At the thought of that little enchantress falling into his hands, helpless and frightened, his excitement surged until his very brain seemed to tremble.

Hearing this, Gurant’s eyes widened slightly, his expression shifting. “Have you been hit so hard that you damaged your brain? That’s a Saintess we’re talking about!”

“I know,” Passat nodded. “But as long as the Saintess violates the rules, Your Grace still has the authority to deal with her, don’t you?”

“…” Gurant fell silent. Under normal circumstances, he would never help Passat. However, he might need the power of the Golden Aslan family in the future, and doing Passat a favor was not entirely out of the question.

‘This church’s Saintess is not of a particularly high rank. Getting rid of her wouldn’t be too difficult.’ After pondering for a moment, Gurant finally made his decision. “Very well. I agree.”

“Your Grace, thank you very much. If there’s ever anything you need from the Golden Aslan family, just say the word. I, Passat of the Holy Church, will do my utmost to satisfy Your Grace!” Passat lifted his wineglass, his face lit with a broad smile.

“Easy enough,” Gurant said as he raised his own glass.

The two then clinked glasses and drained them in one go.

Elsewhere, Irene lay on her bed, her small face pale as anxiety churned within her. She had a strong feeling that Passat would not let her off so easily. “Even though this Saintess position is something I could give up, I still can’t bear to part with it…”

She stared at the ceiling, slowly lifting her right hand and grasping at the empty air. As if she were trying to seize that hazy, intangible future. Yet no matter how hard she tried, she could not grasp it.

“Ahhh! This is so annoying. You bad person[1](#easy-footnote-bottom-1-121612), hurry up and help me deal with this trouble already!” At that moment, Irene suddenly thought of Yae-hime, her heart restless yet inexplicably filled with anticipation. If it were that person, there would surely be a way to solve her troubles.

# **Footnotes:**

1. Syl: What was the term or tone Irene used to refer to Yae-hime again? I remember there was a particular tone but I can’t remember…

+++

# **760 – A Little Knocking and Bumping Works Wonders for Memory Recovery~**

Early morning.

After finishing a set of self-created Taiji outside, Yae-hime returned to the room, lay down on the bed, closed her eyes, and logged into the game.

The morning air in Aoma Village carried a hint of chill. Inside the village chief’s guest room, two little girls were curled up together, still sleeping soundly. Suddenly, a figure appeared on the bed amid a soft white glow.

As if sensing a new source of warmth, the two little girls instinctively leaned over. Using both hands and feet, they clung to Yae-hime like koalas hugging a tree.

“I can’t move…” Their strength was astonishing, clamping onto Yae-hime’s body like a pair of iron pliers. “Forget it. I’ll just keep resting.” After struggling for a moment, she gave up helplessly.

Time flew by, and an hour passed in the blink of an eye.

“Mmm~” Lili slowly opened her eyes, letting out a cute, lazy sound as her expression remained drowsy.

At the same time, Zerene’s eyelashes fluttered, and she gradually opened her clear, watery eyes as well.

“Good morning, Little Hime,” Lili said lazily.

“…” Only then did Zerene realize she was hugging Yae-hime, her small face flushing faintly red. Even so, she showed no intention of letting go.

“Good morning. Could you two let go of me first? My bones are about to fall apart,” Yae-hime said with a look of utter misery. Being hugged to sleep by two beautiful girls was undoubtedly a blissful thing. But there was a prerequisite. Those two beautiful girls had to be soft and weak.

Unfortunately, whether it was Zerene or Lili, both possessed frightening strength. Being hugged by them unconsciously felt like having iron pliers tightening relentlessly around her body. It would be strange if that felt comfortable.

“Sorry, I didn’t mean to,” Lili said, her pretty face reddening as she quickly released her limbs and shifted her body aside.

Seeing this, Zerene hesitated for a moment before imitating her and freeing Yae-hime as well.

“Did you sleep well?” Yae-hime asked as she got up from the bed and looked at the two of them.

“Mm, I slept really comfortably,” Lili said, nodding vigorously.

“Comfortable,” Zerene echoed softly.

Yae-hime reached out and patted Lili’s head, then turned to Zerene. “Did you remember anything?”

“No,” Zerene shook her head. Forget remembering anything. She had not even dreamed. She had slept straight through until morning.

“You’ve lost your memory, and you’re unfamiliar with everything around you. You might as well stay here for now and decide what to do once some of your memories return,” Yae-hime suggested.

After a brief moment of contemplation, Zerene nodded, her expression somewhat dazed. Seeing this, Lili immediately felt a sense of crisis rising within her.

“Little Hime, I heard that for people with amnesia, giving their head a few hard knocks can help them recover very quickly.” She said it with a smile. Yet there was not the slightest warmth in her eyes.

“…” Zerene looked over. Her clear eyes were filled with undisguised surprise, along with a trace of hostility. She sensed an unfriendly aura coming from Lili.
