“That’s a special measure. It shouldn’t be used lightly,” Yae-hime said. She had seen that kind of crude method plenty of times in over-the-top movies and TV dramas. In reality, even smashing someone’s head open would probably not achieve much.

After all, the human brain was incredibly delicate, nothing like old household appliances that could be fixed by giving them a few hard pats.

Hearing this, Zerene immediately let out a sigh of relief. She had genuinely been afraid that Yae-hime would believe that little imp’s words and give her a round of knocking.

“When it comes to memory recovery, stimulation therapy is actually more effective,” Yae-hime said.

“Stimulation therapy?” Lili asked curiously.

“Yes. People with amnesia rarely lose all their memories. Otherwise, they would become no different from a newborn baby,” Yae-hime explained.

Lili nodded. “So?”

“We can use fragments of the amnesiac’s memories to find the things that left the deepest impression and stimulate the brain. By doing so, those scattered memories can be linked together and gradually restored. This process might be quick, or it might take a long time,” Yae-hime said.

“Hey, is there anything you’re afraid of?” After hearing that, Lili immediately turned to Zerene and asked.

“My name isn’t _hey_,” Zerene replied unhappily.

“Do you even have anything you’re afraid of or not?” Lili said, too lazy to argue and pressing on.

“…” That attitude made Zerene feel increasingly displeased.

The atmosphere at the scene instantly grew tense.

Yae-hime rolled her eyes, puzzled inside. Why did these two little ones seem to be at odds with each other?

“Let’s put the matter of memory recovery aside for now.” She reached out and gently patted both of their heads. Then she continued, “Zerene’s body hasn’t fully recovered yet. The most urgent matter is to heal her physically.”

“Alright,” Lili said, withdrawing her gaze and backing down.

Zerene obediently hummed a soft acknowledgment.

“No time to waste. Zerene, lie down,” Yae-hime said as she stood up.

Lili rose as well, while Zerene complied and lay down.

“Alright, Li—Little Hime.” Hesitating for a moment, Zerene still followed Lili’s example and used Yae-hime’s nickname.

At those words, Lili’s small face puffed up slightly, irritation flashing in her eyes. ‘This brat is copying me!’

Yae-hime, however, did not mind at all. After all, Lili was not the only one who called her Little Hime.

At that very moment, far away in the confinement chamber of the royal palace in Jade City, the Seventh Princess, Kastina, suddenly sneezed.

“Who’s badmouthing me?” she muttered in confusion. Inside the vast room, there was no response at all. “Is it just my imagination?” After glancing around, Kastina sat on the bed and gently swung her slender legs.

She looked extremely bored. “Hah… I wonder how Little Hime is doing.” Gazing at the wall not far away, she murmured softly.

---

Elsewhere, the Little Hime whom Kastina missed so dearly had already finished administering acupuncture to Zerene. While repairing her body, Yae-hime also absorbed that lightning energy imbued with profound laws.

After quite some time, the golden bead within her body finished absorbing its allotted share for the day, releasing waves of dazzling light.

‘The lightning energy within Zerene’s body can indeed strengthen this bead. Although the effect is minimal, if this continues, it’s something to look forward to.’

“Mmm~ So comfy, I feel like I’m about to ascend~” At that moment, Zerene, whose body had been filled with life energy, suddenly let out a delighted sound that was all too easy to misunderstand.

It earned Yae-hime a huge eye-roll from Lili standing nearby. If she could, she would have loved to grab the soft flesh on the other girl’s belly and twist it hard!

“What, are your eyes uncomfortable?” Noticing Lili’s look, Yae-hime turned over with a hint of concern.

“Your eyes are the ones with problems!” Lili snapped, kicking out lightly and landing a not-too-heavy kick on Yae-hime.

The latter looked utterly baffled.

After finishing Zerene’s treatment, Yae-hime led the two of them downstairs. At this moment, Angelica had already prepared breakfast.

Seated in the dining hall were Layna and the Fiat siblings, but Angelica’s father was nowhere to be seen.

“Good morning, Princess, Lady Lili, and this adorable little sister. I was just about to call you down for breakfast!” Angelica said with a smile.

“Good morning. Where’s your father?” Yae-hime asked casually.

“Father went out very early. There’s been a lot going on in the village lately, so he needs to take care of things as soon as possible,” Angelica replied.

“That’s hard work indeed,” Yae-hime said as she sat down, speaking while beckoning the two little ones to come over as well.

In Cathay, shared meals were the easiest way to bring people closer together. Usually, after one meal, even strangers would gradually become familiar.

Sure enough, Zerene and Lili soon began competing over food, bickering with great enthusiasm. Seeing this, Yae-hime merely smiled faintly.

+++

# **761 – Irene Prepares to Send Out Her Deluxe Gift Pack**

After the meal. Everyone drank a cup of tea, then officially began the day’s work.

Yae-hime, Layna, and the two little ones worked in the warehouse refining “Holy Water.” Aurora engraved the bottles on the production line next door, while Fiat stood by to assist.

As for Angelica, she went to help her father, who had just recovered, with handling the village’s affairs.

“Cool and chilly… it feels so nice,” Zerene said as she sat on the edge of the pool, her slender legs soaking in the water.

“Soaking your feet really does help relieve fatigue. It’s pretty great,” Lili said as well, sitting on the poolside with her feet immersed.

The emerald-green water reflected their delicate, porcelain-like faces. Beside the two of them, Yae-hime was also soaking… no, correction, at that moment she was earnestly refining what was known as Holy Water.

Once the entire pool had turned a fresh, verdant green, the production line officially started up.

“You all…” Layna rubbed her forehead, looking utterly exasperated as she watched the three of them soaking their feet in the pool.

If outsiders ever found out that the so-called Holy Water was actually three girls’ foot-soaking water, it would probably cause quite a bit of trouble. Of course, some people would be ecstatic. But those kinds of people were, in the end, a minority.

‘Whatever, it’s fine. No one knows anyway.’ With that thought, Layna locked the warehouse doors and silently muttered to herself.

‘Strange… why haven’t those Apostles come to deliver the fragments yet?’ Up on the poolside, Yae-hime wore a puzzled expression. She currently had four Holy Spirit Shards on her. With three more, she would be able to assemble a Sacred Artifact.

A perfect Sacred Artifact could even be stronger than a heavily damaged divine artifact. For example, the Chaos God Ring in her hand. If it were not repaired, it would forever remain at the sub-divine tier. Rather than becoming a true divine artifact.

‘Strictly speaking, the Chaos God Ring has already fallen to the quasi artifact tier.’ Looking at the pitch-black ring in her hand, Yae-hime thought to herself.

Repairing this ring would be far more difficult than gathering seven Holy Spirit Shards.

Being in a phase of rapid growth, she was not particularly focused on that matter. After all, she neither had the time nor knew where to find Chaos Energy to repair the artifact. No matter how she calculated it, collecting Holy Spirit Shards was far more practical.

However, what Yae-hime did not know was that those Apostles were no longer in the Jade Empire. In other words, collecting the remaining fragments was temporarily unrealistic. Unless she deliberately went to the Sky Empire to look for them.

After finishing the refinement of the Holy Water, Yae-hime came down from above with the two little ones.

Layna immediately shot them a massive eye-roll.

“I have something to do later. I’ll be heading back to Jade City for a bit,” Yae-hime said after landing.

“What are you going back to Jade City for?” Lili’s expression changed as she asked worriedly. Given how intense things were right now, returning to the city was clearly an unwise move.

“To have some friends from the church recharge, and to purify this fragment.” As she spoke, Yae-hime took out four fragments from her spatial ring. Three were dull and lifeless, while one emitted a pitch-black aura.

“So that’s what it is,” Lili immediately realized when she saw the fragments. That unusual power her Little Hime had displayed last night had come from these fragments.

Two of them had even been obtained with her help.

“Yes. These fragments are my trump card. They should be a big help with that matter,” Yae-hime said.

“That matter?” Layna asked, confused. She had no idea what Yae-hime was referring to.

“Oh right, I haven’t told you yet,” Yae-hime said, looking at Layna, then glancing at Lili.

The latter gave a gentle nod.

“In a few days, we’re going to counterattack Jade City,” Yae-hime said calmly, staring straight at Layna. It was as if she were talking about something utterly trivial.

But the moment those words left her mouth, it was like a thunderbolt crashing down, leaving Layna’s mind completely blank, unsure how to react. Beside them, Zerene blinked, completely unable to get a word in.

“Really?” Layna finally recovered and asked in a hushed voice.

“Yes. Even pearls aren’t that genuine,” Yae-hime replied with a smile.

“T-That’s just…” Layna clenched her small hands, her body trembling uncontrollably. “That’s way too exciting! Can I take part too?”

When it came to Richard, she had no fondness for him at all. If anything, she harbored a deep-seated resentment toward him. Who asked them to throw her into the dungeon without even bothering to sort out right from wrong in the first place?

“This matter absolutely cannot leak even a hint,” Lili hurriedly warned when she saw how excited Layna looked. Alicia’s rebellion was hardly a secret. Some of the major families who knew the inside story had probably already prepared backup plans. Whoever laughed last, they would side with that person.

What Lili worried about was that the timing of the operation might be accidentally exposed.

“Mhm, I definitely won’t say a word!” Layna nodded in response. Even if Lili had not reminded her, she would not have leaked the slightest bit of information.

“You’ll stay here and handle logistics,” Yae-hime said, lightly patting Layna on the shoulder.

“Logistics, huh…” Layna was clearly a little disappointed.

“With your current strength, going along would just mean watching from the sidelines anyway,” Yae-hime said honestly.

Hearing that, the corner of Layna’s eye twitched. ‘Even if it’s true, you don’t have to say it so bluntly!’ She complained inwardly. Still, she quickly began to feel a bit pleased. The fact that Yae-hime was willing to tell her something this important clearly meant she did not see her as an outsider.

‘Leaving me here for logistics must be because she doesn’t want me taking risks, right? Hehe!’ The more she thought about it, the happier Layna felt.

Zerene, who had been unable to get a word in and did not even know how to, looked utterly bored.

“This isn’t set in stone yet. When it actually starts is still unknown. Just keep it to yourself for now,” Yae-hime said.

Lili gave a small nod.

With the serious matters finished, Yae-hime turned to Zerene and spoke. “Zerene, this is Layna.” She then looked at Layna. “This is Zerene. She’ll be staying in Aoma Village for a while. Make sure you get along.”

“Hello, Zerene,” Layna said with a smile.

“H-Hello, Layna,” Zerene said, hiding behind Yae-hime and peeking out with only half her head visible, looking somewhat shy as she looked at Layna.

That sight made Lili’s small face twitch slightly. ‘Such an act. Where did this little drama queen come from!?’ She absolutely did not believe that this shyness was genuine.

“Like I said earlier, I have something to take care of and need to head back to the city,” Yae-hime said. As she spoke, she gently patted Zerene on the head. “I’ll leave her in your care.”

Before she even finished speaking, Zerene hurriedly grabbed Yae-hime’s hand. “I don’t want you to go!”

In this place, the only one who gave her any sense of closeness was the breathtakingly beautiful presence right in front of her.

“Don’t mess around!” Lili almost instantly rushed over and forcefully knocked Zerene’s hand away.

“You hit me?” Zerene looked at the slightly reddened back of her right hand. Her expression grew serious, and a surge of energy began to stir within her. It looked like she was about to fight Lili.

At that moment, Yae-hime immediately stepped in to mediate. After quite some effort, the two little ones finally made up again. With a bit of soothing, Yae-hime left the church.

“Those two troublemaking little rascals,” she sighed softly along the way, sounding rather exasperated.

Aoma Village was still very quiet. Everyone was doing a good job staying at home. After searching for a while, she found Angelica.

“Princess, you’re done with your work?” Angelica’s face immediately lit up with a smile the moment she appeared.

“More like I came out for some fresh air,” Yae-hime said with a wry smile. She had only one purpose in coming to find Angelica.

+++

# **762 – Dripping with Blood and Filth from Head to Toe**

“By the way, I urgently needed some materials right now. I was wondering whether the chamber of commerce in Aoma Village had any stock.” Yae-hime quickly got straight to the point.

Her purpose in coming to see Angelica was precisely to continue gathering the materials required for the City of Chaos.

Overall, the materials needed for repairs had already been collected. However, certain consumables were required in especially large quantities. It was better to gather as much as possible as early as possible.

After all, the City of Chaos would not remain in the Saint Demon World for very long. Once it returned to Aqua Blue Star, replenishing supplies would require teleporting it to Saint Demon World again. The energy loss incurred during that process was enough to make one’s scalp tingle just thinking about it, and the pain at heart was unavoidable.

Naturally, Yae-hime had no intention of letting such a thing happen. So she made preparations in advance.

“What kind of materials do you need, Princess? Even if we do not have them locally, we will do our utmost to find them!” Angelica said solemnly.

“That will not be necessary. If they can be found, then find them. If not, then forget it.” Yae-hime took out a sheet of paper filled with listed materials from her ring and handed it over.

The required items had already been marked.

Angelica took the paper and hurriedly said, “I will go check with the chamber of commerce immediately!” With that, she swiftly left the scene.

“There really is no need to rush so much.” Yae-hime said. Unfortunately, Angelica could no longer hear her.

After leaving Aoma Village, Yae-hime did not rush back to the city. She went to the docks and looked toward the uninhabited island. “Choosing to descend at this place should be much safer.”

Now that dock operations had been suspended and all nearby villages had been sealed off, the uninhabited island, having just experienced last night’s incident, would not see anyone going there for the time being.

Descending there was undoubtedly the best choice.

“And it is quite far from Jade City. Even if something unexpected happens, Richard will not notice.” She withdrew her gaze, turned around, and stepped forward.

Not long after, the beast carriage at the village entrance sped off toward Jade City.

* **Under the same sky, at the Adventurers’ Guild in Jade City.**

Taurus sat at the round table, one hand resting on its surface while his fingers tapped rhythmically. His expression showed clear impatience. “There is still no news about S.K.Y.?” he asked in a low voice.

At his words, a cadre-level guild member standing in front of him trembled almost imperceptibly. His gaze wandered, his face slightly pale, and he remained silent for a long time.

“I am asking you a question. Did you not hear me?” Taurus stared at him coldly, his tone hostile.

“Young Master Taurus, we have not yet found S.K.Y., but we already have some leads…”

Before he could finish, Taurus slammed the table and stood up, roaring: “Useless trash, all of you are useless trash! So much time has passed and you still cannot even find one person. Am I giving you all that money to do charity!?”

As soon as these words were spoken, the expressions of all the guild members present darkened. Yet not a single person dared to speak up in rebuttal. Because they had signed contracts and were now employees of the Zhang Corporation.

Moreover, those contracts were riddled with hidden, predatory clauses, practically no different from slave contracts. To terminate them, one would have to pay five to six hundred thousand and spend two to three years fighting lawsuits. Otherwise, it was simply impossible.

That momentary greed and vanity back then had cost these people their freedom. Now, whether they swallowed their anger or were shouted at like dogs, it was all the result of their own choices.

Some had tried to sue to terminate their contracts, but under the iron fist of Bestick Legal Firm. Not only did they lose the case, they were also ordered to compensate Zhang Corporation five hundred thousand.

By now, the core members of the Death of Love Guild had long since abandoned any thoughts of escape. They could only endure until their contracts expired before finally leaving.

‘Compared to those who were sued by their companies just for refusing overtime, we are still the lucky ones.’ One of the cadres sighed inwardly, his face showing a complex expression that was neither quite laughter nor quite tears.

“You have five days to find him. If you cannot, you will all regret it!” With his temper fully unleashed, Taurus tore away his usual facade, revealing the lofty, domineering face of a capitalist who looked down on everyone else.

In his eyes, these dirt-poor wretches were all cheap bones. Without beating or scolding, they would never move.

Hearing this, everyone present felt anger they dared not voice. Who else could they blame for signing contracts that sold themselves? Who had made this society recognize nothing but money? Sorry, but in this world, money really could buy the right to do whatever one pleased.

At this very moment, Taurus was the living embodiment of that saying, its walking incarnation.

“Why are you idiots standing around here? Get the hell out there and start looking for him!” With a sweeping motion of his arm, Taurus roared furiously, like an enraged lion.

The lead guild cadre answered with a subdued acknowledgment, then lowered his head and walked out of the guild, both ashamed and furious. His body trembled, his teeth were clenched tight. His heart felt as though it had been bound by iron chains.

At that moment, he felt like a bonded laborer who had lost even the qualification to be treated as a human being.

The same loss of qualification applied to the pile of players following behind him. Their situation perfectly fit that old saying: there was no such thing as a free lunch in this world.

And of course, there was also this one: all crows under heaven were equally black.

Money itself was something without conscience, without humanity. Coveting the petty benefits offered by money would only make one lose their freedom, lose the very right to be human. At this moment, they understood it. They saw it clearly. But it was already too late.

Inside the Adventurers’ Guild, Taurus slowly sat back down. The anger in his heart gradually dissipated, and his expression eased somewhat.

Only then did Vanessa, who had been sitting opposite him in silence all this time, finally speak, “Aren’t you afraid they might turn against you?”

Following her voice, Taurus looked over and bared his teeth in a grin, speaking with domineering confidence, “These dirt-poor wretches already have collars fastened around their necks by me. Turning against me? That would only end with their families ruined and their homes destroyed!”

“It would be better to be a bit more refined in how you conduct yourself.” Vanessa took a sip of her now-cold tea and said flatly.

“Heh, listen to you talk. As if your Yang family were some great benefactors!” Taurus said with disdain. Ever since being stabbed in the back by S.K.Y., the only thing left in his heart had been a raging inferno of anger.

That tiny trace of romantic feeling from before had long since vanished. Now, when facing Vanessa, it was as if he were looking at a hollow shell of flesh. His heart felt nothing at all.

“What kind of family the Yangs are is not for you to judge.” Vanessa set down her teacup and stood up, her expression utterly calm. She seemed completely unaffected by the barbs in his words.

“Taurus, our cooperation ends here. From this day forward, the Death of Flower Guild and the Death of Love Guild will have nothing more to do with each other.” Her purpose in logging in today had been precisely to draw a clear line between herself and Taurus.

“What did you say!?” Taurus suddenly widened his eyes and shouted in disbelief.

“Our two guilds are formally cutting ties today. From now on, we will mind our own business and keep to our own waters.” Vanessa said coolly, neither heated nor cold.

“Even you are betraying me!?” Upon hearing this, Taurus clenched his fists tightly and roared, his face twisting in fury.

“Betrayal? Taurus, aren’t you mistaken about something? From the very beginning, we were nothing more than partners.” Vanessa let out a cold laugh, then opened her interface and clicked the logout button.

Watching her disappear in a flash of white light, Taurus was so furious that his entire face flushed red, then darkened. In the end, he slammed his fist heavily onto the tabletop, smashing the round table to pieces.

Elsewhere, inside the beast carriage racing toward Jade City, Yae-hime lounged comfortably as she browsed forum posts.

“Capitalists could never have a conscience. If they sign you at a high price, it is obviously to squeeze you dry.”

Looking at the forum thread flooding the front page titled [Prodigal Master of Huadu’s Tyrannical Contract], she could not help but mutter to herself.

+++

# **763 – Anomaly in Kun Ruins, A New Threat Emerges!**

At this moment, the Linhnan Server Forum looked nothing like its usual self. Posts laced with frustration and anger sprang up like mushrooms after the rain. The atmosphere made people feel inexplicably irritated.

Every one of those posts shared a single theme: oppressive capitalism.

“Even if you scream yourselves hoarse here, no one can actually help you,” Yae-hime said flatly.

The ruthlessness and terror of capitalism were things one could only truly understand after experiencing them firsthand. Only then would you realize just how powerless you were in front of it.

“Trying to reason with capitalism using the law, filing lawsuits, even if you win, it’s no different from losing.”

After all, the legal teams raised by capitalists had a hundred ways to drag you to death. Yae-hime had once seen workers who tried to defend their rights through lawsuits end up with nothing at all.

Capitalists had time and money to stall, but the proletariat did not. Drag it out for a year or two. Your job would be gone. Your family would fall apart. What was the point of winning then?

Such an exorbitant cost of defending one’s rights was enough to make anyone back away.

“And besides… forget it. It has nothing to do with me anyway.” Yae-hime shook her head and casually closed the post. Her gaze shifted downward, landing on a freshly surfaced hot thread.

“Did the Death of Love Guild fall out with the Death of Flower Guild?”

After opening the thread and skimming through it, she could not help but frown in confusion. From the content, it seemed that Vanessa had already gone her separate way from Taurus. Yet as for why they split, the poster’s explanation was frustratingly vague.

“Together, they could be considered a force that can’t be ignored. Splitting up like this actually benefits me. At the very least, I won’t have to worry about being ambushed jointly anymore.” Although Yae-hime could easily deal with them, having one less problem for no reason at all was still a good thing.

As for whether the post was true or not, she could not be bothered to verify it.

Outside, the beast carriage continued racing toward Jade City at high speed.

---

At the same time. At Mount Heavenspine.

This foremost sacred mountain, revered as the ancestral dragon vein of Cathay, was undergoing subtle changes. Deep within the mountain range of the Emeraldreach, the surrounding space suddenly rippled, like a calm lake disturbed by a thrown stone, sending wave after wave of oscillations outward.

Immediately afterward, a surge of spatial power spread, and at the center of the ripples, a gap tore open. No, rather than a gap, it looked more like a door.

With a sharp swish, two black silhouettes shot out like streaks of lightning. The instant they touched the ground, the door snapped shut, and the ripples vanished at once.

Space gradually returned to normal. As if nothing unusual had ever happened. Yet the two men standing there, straight as spears, were like irrefutable evidence, silently testifying to the anomaly that had just occurred.

At the same moment, within the City of Chaos.

“Little Blue, a singularity just registered a high-energy reaction!” Vera 18 exclaimed excitedly as she stared at the floating panel.

“What kind of high-energy reaction?” Little Blue drifted over, asking curiously. Crumbs still clung to the corner of her mouth, making it painfully obvious that she had been sneaking snacks.

“Little Blue, how can you eat everything by yourself!” Vera 18 protested indignantly when she noticed what looked suspiciously like meat crumbs.

The other Vera clones followed the sound and, sure enough, caught sight of the evidence of Little Blue’s secret snacking. Without another word, they immediately surrounded her to demand an explanation.

“Slander! Y-you can’t just smear my innocence out of thin air!” Little Blue hurriedly retorted as she faced the five of them encircling her.

“This is the proof!” Vera 18 shot out her hand, pinching the crumbs at the corner of Little Blue’s mouth with lightning speed. She then pulled her hand back and stared straight at her, pressing relentlessly. “You still want to deny it?”

Seeing this, Little Blue’s eyes darted about, two rosy clouds blooming on her cute little face as she argued back stubbornly. “F-food connoisseurs’ matters don’t count as stealing! A true gourmand…”

What followed was a string of hard-to-understand rambling. Something about gourmands risking their lives to sample a hundred flavors and the like. The others listened with frosty expressions, irritation welling up in their hearts.

While everyone else was busy, she had actually sneaked off to the side to secretly snack. It was utterly outrageous!

Nominally, Little Blue was their superior. But in Yae-hime’s eyes, they were equals. There was no hierarchy between them. As a result, these little ones were not the least bit afraid of Little Blue.

“Tsk, fine, I’ll share some with you, okay!” Seeing the way they looked ready to devour her alive, Little Blue could only surrender helplessly.

“That’s more like it!” the five Vera sisters replied in unison. Right after that, the little group huddled together, happily enjoying the snacks Little Blue had secretly hoarded.

After a whirlwind of eating that left nothing behind, they returned to their respective posts, thoroughly satisfied.

“Number Eighteen, what was that high-energy reaction you mentioned earlier?” Only then did Little Blue finally remember what had happened before.

“Ah, I almost forgot.” Vera 18 patted her head, then lightly tapped the floating panel and pulled up the anomalous data for her to see.

“The data from that singularity spiked sharply for an instant, then quickly dropped back to normal levels. It just feels… strange.” Little Blue stared at the abnormal readings, her expression turning noticeably more serious.

“What’s strange about it?” Vera 18 asked.

“I don’t really know either,” Little Blue said, spreading her hands.

Vera 18 immediately rolled her eyes at her.

“Let’s wait until Master comes out later and study it together,” Little Blue said.

“All right.” Vera 18 nodded, lightly touching the screen again as she continued monitoring the changes at the singularity.

Off to the side, Little Blue drifted back to her workstation, putting on a show of working hard.

---

At the foot of Mount Heavenspine, two figures suddenly flashed into existence. Sunlight fell upon them, dissolving the peculiar aura of mystery around their bodies and revealing their true appearances.

They were two men.

The man on the left looked to be around fifty years old and stood roughly 180 centimeters tall. He wore a gray robe, his long hair hanging loose over his shoulders. His features were plain and slightly gaunt, with his temples noticeably bulging on both sides. His hands were rough, like the bark of an old pine tree.

The man on the right appeared to be seventeen or eighteen, standing about 185 centimeters tall and dressed in a high-quality white robe. He was handsome, with sharp, heroic brows and bright, spirited eyes, a piercing presence radiating from him.

“Just like the rumors said. The air of the outside world is so turbid it’s hard to breathe,” the handsome youth said with a deep frown, his expression clearly displeased.

“It’s acceptable,” the middle-aged man replied coldly.

“Senior Brother Lucen, why do you always wear that bitter, sour face? It looks awful,” the youth said with a grin as he glanced over.

“I was born this way. Enough idle talk. We didn’t enter the secular world this time for sightseeing.”

“Tch, of all people, Master had to pick someone as dull as you to accompany me. He’s really gone too far,” the youth said, spreading his hands with a helpless look.

“It’s precisely because I’m this dull that I can keep you in check. Junior Brother Axiom, the main purpose of our descent this time is to investigate the cause of the anomaly. Don’t stir up any trouble for me and waste time and energy for no reason,” the man called Lucen warned.

“Got it, got it,” the youth called Axiom replied impatiently.

“Axiom, this is your first time entering the secular world. You only have a shallow understanding of many mundane matters. As your senior brother—”

“That’s enough! You’ve said this eight hundred times already!” Axiom clutched his head and shouted in agony. Everything about this senior brother was fine, except for his habit of endlessly nagging. It was like a fly buzzing around his ears, making him want nothing more than to grab it, rip it open, pull out its guts, wrap them around its neck, and yank hard!

“Then the world would finally be peaceful!”

“Peaceful in what way?”

“Nothing!”

“Oh right, Senior Brother Lucen, where are we heading next?” Axiom hurriedly changed the subject.

“Yanjing.”

“By that thing called a train?” Axiom asked again.

“We’ll run there.”

The moment Lucen said that, Axiom nearly collapsed on the spot. Because from Emeraldreach to Yanjing, the distance was a full 1,700 kilometers.

+++

# **764 – Arrogant Axiom, Calm Lucen**

“Senior Brother Lucen, you’re joking, right?!” Axiom steadied himself and asked urgently. Although he was not some pampered young master, he still could not withstand that kind of ordeal.

“Joking? There was no such thing. This was precisely how the Profound Truth Sect practiced worldly training. If you do not roll around in the mortal world, how can you see through it and attain transcendence?” Lucen said solemnly.

“I understand the reasoning, but this place is so far from Yanjing. Running all the way there would cripple me!” Axiom said heatedly. It was his first time leaving Kun Ruins to enter the outside world, but he was not completely ignorant of external affairs.

After all, Kun Ruins was not truly isolated from the world beyond. From time to time, a few practitioners would venture out. While tempering themselves, they would also bring back information from the outside world.

“I never said you had to run there in a single day,” Lucen replied calmly.

“I know that, but entering the world doesn’t mean living like an ascetic, does it?” Axiom said with dissatisfaction.

“Strictly speaking, it is indeed no different from the life of an ascetic. From this moment on, your food, clothing, shelter, and travel must all be handled by yourself. In addition, you are forbidden from using force to coerce others into doing things for you. Entering the world is meant for you to experience the many facets of life and see through mortal attachments. External assistance brings harm rather than benefit.” Lucen explained.

“You want me to live like those mortals, enduring hardship!?” Hearing this, Axiom’s eyes widened, and his handsome features twisted slightly.

“You seem to have misunderstood something.” Lucen raised a hand and pressed it downward, signaling him to calm down. “What kind of life you live in the outside world depends entirely on your own efforts. You can become a laborer, or you can become a wealthy man. As long as there is no external help, you may live any life you choose. Also, rein in that arrogance of yours. Even in the outside world, there are individuals far stronger than you.”

“Stronger than me? Senior Brother Lucen must be joking, right? I am a peerless prodigy of the Profound Truth Sect, with one foot already stepping into the Innate Realm! With such a filthy and chaotic environment out there, how could anyone possibly surpass me?” Axiom laughed in disbelief.

He had grown up in Kun Ruins, where spiritual energy was abundant. Even before he began training, his body had been constantly tempered in medicinal baths brewed from precious herbs.

He soaked in them until the age of ten, when he formally entered the Profound Truth Sect and became a new generation inner disciple. At twelve, he stepped into the Master level. At fourteen, he reached the peak Master level. At fifteen, he entered the Grandmaster Realm. At sixteen, he achieved Grandmaster Great Perfection. Now, at eighteen, he already had one foot stepped into that legendary realm.

Such a cheat-like growth trajectory did indeed justify the title of prodigy. As for being a peerless prodigy, even he admitted he had not quite earned that qualification.

“The cultivation conditions in the outside world are indeed harsh, but that does not mean it has no advantages. With a population of several billion, it is inevitable that some monster-level individuals will emerge. Cathay’s Lisa, as well as Arthur, Lilith, and Plato overseas, are all of this caliber. Like you, some of them entered that realm even earlier. Moreover, their combat experience is something you can never hope to match.” Lucen said indifferently.

“…” Hearing this, Axiom fell silent. It was obvious that he had harbored serious misconceptions about the outside world before this.

‘Such an environment could still give birth to figures like that. It’s truly inconceivable! If they were to cultivate in Kun Ruins, then…’ At that moment, Axiom was deeply shaken.

“There are three objectives for our journey this time. First, investigate the cause of the anomalies in the outside world. Second, undergo worldly training. Third, seek out outstanding seedlings and bring them back to Kun Ruins.” Lucen said.

“Outstanding seedlings? Aren’t we supposed to bring back those powerful individuals instead?” Axiom asked in confusion.

Lucen shook his head. “Those in the outside world who currently possess strength comparable to yours are all relatively old, with limited potential. Moreover, having started from such high foundations, they would have no sense of belonging to the Kun Ruins at all. Bringing them back would do more harm than good.”

“So that’s how it is.” Axiom nodded, finally feeling reassured. “By the way, Senior Brother Lucen, you’re far stronger than those people in the outside world, right?”

“That is only natural,” Lucen replied calmly. As his guardian, his strength was inevitably far greater than Axiom’s. “Even though we are all within the same realm, there are still clear distinctions. For example, it may look like you and I are both on the first layer. In reality, only you are on the first layer. I, on the other hand, am on the fifth.”

“Master never told me there were differences like this within the realm.” Axiom curled his lips, speaking with some dissatisfaction.

“Since Master chose not to tell you, there was naturally a reason. See? Hasn’t some of that arrogance of yours already been worn down?” Lucen said with a faint smile.

“…” Axiom was left speechless.

“Enough idle talk. Let’s set off.” Lucen reined in his expression and looked toward the distance.

Those words made Axiom roll his eyes inwardly. ‘Enough idle talk? You’re the one who’s talked the most today!’

“Go!” Lucen gave a light shout, and his figure shot forward like a cannonball leaving its barrel. Along the way, sand, stones, grass, and leaves were blasted into the air by the violent aftershock.

Seeing this, Axiom frowned and said in a low voice, “Are you rushing off to reincarnate or something?”[1](#easy-footnote-bottom-1-121634)

As his words fell, he followed after Lucen with a contemplative expression.

‘How dare mere outsiders claim to be stronger than me! Just wait. In less than half a month, I’ll crush you all and make you bow in submission!’

As a prodigy of the Kun Ruins, Axiom did not rein in the arrogance in his heart because of Lucen’s words. He would prove here that he was the strongest!

---

Inside the game.

Yae-hime naturally had no idea about the upheavals in the outside world. After stepping down from the beast carriage, she raised a hand to shield her eyes from the vicious sunlight.

She was already very close to Jade City.

“You can head back now.”

“Yes, Lord Angel!” The coachman bowed respectfully, then returned to his seat and drove the carriage away.

Watching the beast carriage gradually disappear into the distance, Yae-hime withdrew her gaze and looked toward the majestic Jade City.

“Next… should I go to Allie’s place first, or Irene’s… Wait, that’s not even the issue. I don’t have enough time to handle both matters!” Treating Allie would take a considerable amount of time, and assisting Irene with the purification and recharging of the Holy Spirit Shards would also require no small effort.

“I can’t stay in Jade City for too long.” Yae-hime bit her lip, feeling a slight headache. Because of Richard, she could not afford to risk lingering in Jade City. Actually, coming back here at all was already a risky move. The longer she stayed, the greater the danger.

After pondering for a moment, a flash of inspiration suddenly crossed her mind. “Why am I so fixated on treating Allie inside the city? Wouldn’t it be fine if she secretly slipped out to Aoma Village instead?”

Earlier, she had clearly fallen into a mental blind spot, assuming that Allie, like Irene, could not easily leave Jade City. In reality, only Irene was unable to leave. Allie was merely unwilling to.

“Once I get back, I’ll have Lili send someone to explain the situation to Allie. That settles the problem perfectly.” Yae-hime nodded in satisfaction.

In truth, after thinking it through carefully, she felt that performing the final treatment inside the city was not a good idea. Who knew whether a fully recovered Allie might draw Richard’s attention?

After weighing it again and again, handling it outside was clearly safer. Having made up her mind, Yae-hime immediately took action. With a light tap of her toe against the ground, her figure leapt forward. In the next instant, her silhouette vanished into the void, disappearing completely.

# **Footnotes:**

1. Syl: Fun fact, 赶去投胎 (Gǎn qù tóutāi) is a famous Chinese saying of cursing someone. I said it a lot whenever someone sped past me on the road.

+++

# **765 – Unexpected Complications**

“I couldn’t fall asleep…” Irene lay on the bed, muttering to herself. Her small face looked a little pale, her expression drained. Faint dark circles rimmed her eyes, and the red veins within them stood out clearly. It was obvious that she had not slept a wink all night.

“No matter how I think about it, I can’t come up with a perfect solution. My head hurts so badly!” Irene rolled back and forth on the bed, complaining irritably. She had never imagined that simply stepping outside for a moment would land her in such a huge mess.

If she had known that Passat and his group would come to the church and end up clashing with her, Irene would never have gone out, no matter what. After all, most of the time she stayed inside the church, shut away in her room, appreciating her little lewd nove—no, those were great works of literature!

“Ahhh, this is so annoying. At least let me read a novel to calm my nerves!” As long as she immersed herself in the world of fiction, she could forget all the troubles of reality. Unfortunately, all of Irene’s treasured books were with Yae-hime. If the other party did not come over, she would not get to read a single page.

“You bad girl, you bad girl! Why aren’t you here yet!”

“Who are you calling a bad girl?”

Suddenly, a second voice rang out in the room.

In the first second, Irene was so startled that her heart nearly stopped. At one and a half seconds, her mind latched onto a familiar voice. At the second second, her shock turned into joy. At two and a half seconds, her smile bloomed, delight flooding her face. By the third second, Irene sprang up and lunged toward the source of the sound.

“Bad girl, you’re finally here… wah!” At three and a half seconds, she crashed onto the floor. “Wuuuh, why did you dodge!”

“With my small frame, if you pounced on me like that, I’d definitely end up breaking a few bones.” Yae-hime spoke from the side, a faint smile appearing on her face. “That aside, what kind of trouble did you run into? You didn’t even notice me coming in.”

Hearing that, Irene immediately hugged Yae-hime’s legs. “Princess, you have to help me think of a solution!” As she spoke, her large eyes brimmed with crystalline tears.

“Did something really happen?” Yae-hime asked, puzzled.

With Irene’s strength, while she could not exactly run rampant in Jade City, she was not someone who could be bullied so easily either.

“Yes, yes. I’m suffering so much!” Irene nodded vigorously.

“Get up first. Let’s talk properly.”

“Princess, this time I really can only rely on you!” Irene quickly let go and stood up, the dejected look on her face instantly vanishing.

“Even though I don’t know what it is yet, I’ll do my best.” Yae-hime sat down on the bed and said calmly.

Anything that could give Irene this much of a headache was certainly not simple. Whether she could actually help was still uncertain, so naturally she did not make any promises.

Irene bounced over and plopped down beside Yae-hime, speaking excitedly. “It’s like this…” After fifteen full minutes, she finally explained the entire sequence of events from beginning to end.

“Kill him,” Yae-hime said expressionlessly.

“If I could, I’d kill him right now!” Irene snapped angrily, then immediately wilted again. “Too bad I can’t…”

“The Southern Grand Church and the Golden Aslan family really are troublesome,” Yae-hime nodded.

“Princess, hurry up and think of a solution that satisfies everyone!” Irene grabbed Yae-hime’s hand, looking pitiful.

After pondering for a moment, the latter said, “Then don’t take the position of Saintess.”

“No! The Saintess identity is very important to me!” Irene shook her head fiercely.

“I see. That makes it a bit troublesome.” For a moment, even Yae-hime could not think of a good solution.

“Princess, you have to help me!” At that moment, panic surged in Irene’s heart. If even her bad girl had no way out, then what was she supposed to do?

“Give me a few more days. I’ll see if I can conveniently get rid of him.” Yae-hime said it lightly, as if she were talking about something utterly trivial.

Hearing this, Irene blinked, then exclaimed in shock, “Are you crazy?! Passat is a cleric of the Southern Grand Church, and he’s also from the Golden Aslan family. We can’t afford to provoke him! Even if we could, with your strength, you still wouldn’t be able to get rid of him!”

“In this world, there is no one I can’t afford to provoke.” Yae-hime looked at Irene calmly and spoke in an indifferent tone. At that moment, her figure seemed to grow impossibly large in Irene’s eyes.

‘What’s going on… Her strength is clearly inferior to mine. So why does she give off such an overwhelming, unquestionable presence, as if no matter how great the difficulty, nothing could stop her?’ Irene stared straight at her, her heartbeat quickening.

“Relax. I’ll take care of this matter.” Yae-hime reached out and gently stroked her head. “No one can take away your position as Saintess.”

That gentle gesture and those reassuring words made Irene feel completely at ease. Without realizing it, she leaned against Yae-hime, her eyes slowly closing as she drifted into sleep.

Hearing the faint, steady rhythm of her breathing, Yae-hime’s expression changed for a brief moment before quickly returning to normal.

“You’ve really had it rough.” She said softly. Then, she carefully laid Irene down on the bed. “It looks like today won’t work.”

Plans never kept up with changes, and Yae-hime could only smile helplessly.

“Zzz… Zzz…” On the bed, Irene slept soundly, her slightly pale face wearing a faint, peaceful smile.

“Get some good rest. I’ll come see you tomorrow…” As Yae-hime said this and prepared to get up, a small hand suddenly grabbed her. She tried to pry those fingers open, only to find that she could not move them at all. It was as if they were clamped shut by a pair of iron pincers.

“…” Now, leaving was no longer an option. At this moment, two choices surfaced in Yae-hime’s mind. First, wake Irene up. Second, lie down and rest.

Looking at the peaceful expression on Irene’s face and the faint dark circles beneath her eyes, she immediately crossed out the first option. However, if she did not wake Irene, she would have to stay in the church, stay in Jade City. At least until Irene woke up.

During that time, the risks she faced would be far from trivial. Under normal circumstances, waking Irene and having her let her leave would undoubtedly be the safer choice. Yet, the moment she saw that adorable sleeping face, Yae-hime found herself unable to do it. How could she not tell that Irene had been awake all night?

“Forget it. Richard probably doesn’t have the time to come looking for anyone right now anyway.” Yae-hime slowly lay down and murmured to herself.

From Irene’s account, combined with what she had seen while sneaking in herself, she reached a conclusion. Richard had sold out his country. To deal with Alicia, he intended to ally with the Holy Empire.

Such an alliance never came without a price. As an empire ruled by imperial authority, the church within the Jade Empire had never held much power.

“If these clerics really came to support Richard, then Richard would definitely have to funnel certain benefits to them.”

By allowing an external power to intervene in this affair, even if Alicia was ultimately dealt with, Richard would still have to pay a considerable price to the Holy Empire. This was outright treason.

“The bishop of the Southern Grand Church, Passat of the Holy Church, along with several hundred powerful clerics… Just thinking about it gives me a headache.” Staring up at the somewhat aged ceiling, Yae-hime said with a slight frown.

+++

# **766 – No Favors Without a Catch**

The sun outside was still vicious, and the streets of Jade City were far quieter than they usually were around mealtime.

Most of those on the road were ordinary pedestrians, while the wolfish patrols of guards seen days earlier had thinned out considerably. They had probably given up on the search. Or perhaps there was simply no longer any need to continue it.

The guards now stationed around the area were merely the usual on-duty personnel. Seeing these familiar faces at last put people somewhat at ease. They no longer had to live in constant fear as they had over the past few days.

Inside Irene’s room, Yae-hime stood rigid, her nerves taut and her heartbeat racing. Because outside the door stood a powerful presence.

**Knock, knock, knock.**

Suddenly, that powerful presence knocked heavily on the door. Even though it was clearly a casual knock, the aura it carried was still deeply intimidating.

Yae-hime forcibly calmed herself and suppressed her presence to the absolute minimum. For someone who possessed basic spatial power, concealing her aura and sense of existence was not particularly difficult.

The knocking abruptly stopped. After standing outside for a moment, the person turned and left Irene’s room. Yae-hime did not move at all, as though she had merged completely with the surrounding space.

With a sharp swish, the figure that had just left suddenly reappeared in front of the door.

“Strange. Could I have sensed it wrong?” the man murmured in a low voice.

Under the sunlight, his face was finally revealed. It was Gurant, the bishop of the Southern Grand Church. As soon as he finished speaking, he turned and left. This time, he truly departed.

Inside the room, Yae-hime finally let out a breath of relief. “Phew… That terrifying aura must be the bishop Irene mentioned. The helper Richard brought in is no ordinary figure.” She tilted her head toward the door and spoke softly.

The opponent’s strength was clearly far beyond what she had initially expected.

“He’s probably about on par with Lili.” Without having truly crossed hands with him, Yae-hime could not determine just how high Gurant’s upper limit was. She could only make a rough estimate.

“That guy doesn’t seem like he came specifically to see Irene.” Staring at the door, Yae-hime spoke with a puzzled expression. If he truly had business with Irene, how could he have left so easily?

“He was probably just passing by and acted on a whim.” With no further information, she could not infer Gurant’s true intentions at all.

“Uuu… mm…” At that moment, Irene, who was lying on the bed, let out a lazy, sleepy sound. She then slowly opened her eyes.

“You’re awake.” Yae-hime looked over and smiled.

“… ” Irene blinked, her rusted brain finally starting to turn. Within a few seconds, she grasped the situation. So she had fallen asleep without realizing it.

‘She actually stayed by my side the whole time. That bad girl is unexpectedly considerate.’ Thinking this, she could not help but smile happily.

“Are you hungry?” Yae-hime asked while reaching out to tidy Irene’s messy hair.

Hearing that, Irene felt as though her heart were about to melt.

‘So considerate! Is this bad girl really the bad girl I knew?’ She could not help but doubt it.

“Not hungry?” Yae-hime asked again. Her voice was as gentle as flowing water.

“I am.” Irene nodded, a faint blush blooming across her cheeks.

“I’ll co—” Yae-hime started to say, then suddenly remembered that there was no kitchen in Irene’s room.

“Co?” Irene asked, sounding slightly confused.

“No, I mean, next time we get the chance, I’ll personally cook you a bowl of noodles.” Yae-hime said.

“I see.”

“Mm. For now, let’s just keep it simple. That said, could you let go of my hand?” Yae-hime lowered her head and looked at her own arm as she spoke. On it was a fair, delicate little hand.

“How strange. Why am I holding your hand?” Irene said in surprise. She had been holding it so naturally that she had not sensed anything amiss.

“You kept holding onto my hand the whole time after you fell asleep,” Yae-hime said irritably. ‘Did she seriously have no self-awareness at all?’

“Ah!” Irene hurriedly let go, an embarrassed expression instantly creeping onto her small face. “I… I didn’t do it on purpose…” She lowered her voice, speaking with a hint of awkwardness.

“It’s fine.” Yae-hime shook her head lightly. She then took out a large assortment of pastries from her spatial ring, along with a teapot of rather unusual structure.

“Wait a moment. I’ll brew a pot of tea.” As she spoke, Yae-hime took out another item from the spatial ring and handed it to Irene. It was a beautifully made book.

“This is!?” Seeing the familiar cover and the familiar text, Irene could not help but exclaim.

“The second half. You’ve been waiting a long time for it, haven’t you?” Yae-hime said with a calm smile. The book in her hands was none other than the brand-new masterpiece by Alicia that she and Irene had enjoyed together before.

“Wuuah, I missed you so much!” Irene excitedly snatched the lewd novel from Yae-hime’s hands and hugged it tightly to her chest. She felt as if she had not read a lewd novel for half a lifetime, and the hunger in her heart was almost unbearable.

At the same time, a wave of emotion surged up from deep within her. ‘Today, that bad girl is being so gentle and considerate. If only she were like this every day!’

Watching Yae-hime busy herself at the small dining table, the warmth in Irene’s heart grew even stronger.

Fifteen minutes later. Yae-hime had finished brewing a pot of fine black tea. The delicious pastries were neatly arranged on plates, looking tempting enough to make anyone’s mouth water.

Reluctantly, Irene set the lewd novel aside and enjoyed afternoon tea together with Yae-hime. A cozy, gentle atmosphere spread throughout the room. Moments like these always passed far too quickly.

After finishing the last sip of fragrant tea, Irene returned to the bed in satisfaction, ready to continue reading her lewd novel. However, before she could even open the book, Yae-hime pressed it down with one hand.

“You slept well, ate well, drank well, and were taken care of. Today, I already fulfilled four of your wishes in one go.”

“Huh?” Hearing this, Irene tilted her head in confusion.

“Irene, we’re good friends, right?” Yae-hime did not explain further and instead looked straight at her.

“Y-yes! We are, good friends!” Stared at by those captivating eyes, Irene immediately became flustered.

“Good friends should help each other, shouldn’t they?” Yae-hime said gently.

“Yes.” Irene nodded.

“Was I good to you today?”

“Mhm!” Irene nodded again.

“Good. Now it’s your turn to be good to me.”

Before the words finished leaving her mouth, Yae-hime took four fragments out of her spatial ring and placed them in front of Irene. The moment Irene saw the fragments, her eyes and the corners of her mouth twitched faintly.

Then she reached out with both hands, firmly grabbing Yae-hime by the shoulders as she roared, “Didn’t I tell you to use them sparingly!?”

“Ahahaha, I ran into some trouble, so I ended up using up all the energy,” Yae-hime said awkwardly.

“Ugh, bad girl, I hate you!” Irene puffed out her cheeks slightly as she spoke. How could she not understand now? All that earlier gentleness and consideration had just been currying favor.

‘Give me back my feelings!’

“Please,” Yae-hime said earnestly, gently patting her head.

“Hmph, only this once!” Irene snorted, clearly having vented much of her anger.

“Mm. I’ll be more careful next time,” Yae-hime promised.

‘If that’s even possible… Well, her promise was completely unreliable anyway.’

“Wait, why is there an extra one!?” After counting the fragments on the bed, Irene exclaimed in surprise.

“It’s like this…” Yae-hime hurriedly explained the origin of the fourth fragment.

After listening, Irene glanced again at the jet-black fragment, which was clearly larger than the other three, and said in a low voice, “Maybe I should just quietly slip it away.”

+++

# **767 – Plenty of Perks, Sister Red Returns**

“Did you just say something?” Yae-hime leaned in, her pretty face almost pressing against Irene’s small face, smiling with narrowed eyes as she spoke.

“W-wah!” The latter was startled badly, her body jerking backward as she hurriedly cried out.

“Why are you so flustered? Do you have a guilty conscience?” Yae-hime continued smiling as she asked.

“N-no, I don’t! I walk straight and stand upright. There’s nothing guilty about me at all!” Irene steadied herself and shot back in protest.

“Since there isn’t, then let’s begin.”

“Uuugh, you bad person!” Staring at the four fragments lying on the bed, Irene spoke with a near-tearful expression. This workload was clearly meant to squeeze her dry.

“Relax. I’ll fully support you,” Yae-hime said as she sat down, offering reassurance.

Hearing that, Irene finally let out a breath of relief. With Yae-hime providing full assistance, things would definitely be much easier.

“Th-then let’s start right away!” She picked up the pitch-black fragment and placed it in her palm, her expression turning solemn.

On the other side, Yae-hime removed her boots and moved behind Irene. Her pale, jade-like hand extended forward and gently pressed against Irene’s smooth back. In the next instant, green flames ignited across her entire palm as life energy surged forth.

‘Uu… my body is going to be filled again~’

Sensing the endless stream of life energy pouring into her body, Irene’s face flushed slightly, her heart racing with excitement. In the blink of an eye, the stamina she had burned away during her sleepless nights was fully restored.

After internally converting the energy into sacred power, Irene officially began purifying the fragment in her palm. Golden light blossomed as the pitch-black fragment immediately began releasing wisps of dark mist.

The two worked in seamless coordination, and in less than twenty minutes, the fragment was completely purified. At this moment, the fragment in Irene’s hand had turned crystal clear, faint traces of holy power seeping out.

‘I can feel it. It’s a holy power that resonates extremely well with me!’ Clutching the fragment tightly, a pleased smile unconsciously tugged at the corners of her lips. Although helping Yae-hime recharge was exhausting and troublesome work, it was not without its benefits.

As long as she could comprehend the power within, Irene could step into a higher tier altogether. The legendary realm was no longer just a dream.

Suppressing the excitement surging in her heart, she and Yae-hime resumed their work. This time, it was charging the fragment.

“…” Throughout the process, Yae-hime did not utter a single word. Her expression remained tense as she carefully controlled the output of life energy. Any excessive disturbance could very well attract the attention of that bishop.

She had no intention of becoming the other party’s enemy for now. If they could avoid crossing paths, it was naturally better to do so. Moreover, this kind of meticulous control over life energy brought her no small benefit in her own practice.

While the two were busy, in real life. The Southern Sea Region, Doom Island.

A large fishing vessel was docked at a crude pier. Calling it a pier was generous. It was merely a flattened boulder connected to the island.

“Why isn’t she out yet?” At the bow of the ship stood a dark-skinned, skinny man in his forties. His name was Mack. On the surface, he was a fisherman. In reality, he was a smuggler who operated across Southeast Asia, specializing in illegal border crossings between nearby countries.

At this moment, he was waiting for Sister Red to come out. She was an old client of his and paid extremely well.

“That woman is really dragging her feet,” a sailor complained irritably. On an eerie island like this, he did not want to stay even half a minute longer. What’s more, there were rumors that all kinds of lethal venomous creatures lived there. If a few of them crawled out, it would be more than enough to ruin their day.

“But she pays a lot,” Mack said with a shrug, sounding helpless. Just like his men, he had no desire whatsoever to get close to this island. As a professional smuggler, Mack was well aware of the situation around Southeast Asia.

Doom Island was the most dangerous place in the entire region. Venomous insects and poisonous miasma were not just rumors. He had once helped several desperate fugitives land on the island. Not long after, shrill screams echoed from within. In the end, only one person managed to escape alive.

Even now, Mack could still vividly recall the despair on that man’s face and the terrified words he uttered before dying.

“Bugs. Huge bugs. Help.”

“Captain, what huge bugs?” A sailor on deck asked in confusion.

“Nothing,” Mack shook his head. “Just remembered something from the past.”

‘That woman can go in and out of Doom Island without a scratch… truly intriguing.’ He vaguely sensed that Sister Red was anything but ordinary. If she had not repeatedly assured him that those insects would never leave Doom Island, he would never have wanted to come to this cursed place.

“Captain, the woman in red is coming out!” At that moment, a sharp-eyed sailor spotted a flash of red within the dense forest and shouted.

“When she comes over, you are to call her Sister Red,” Mack reminded them.

A woman who could freely enter and leave Doom Island was clearly someone formidable. He had no intention of courting death because of his subordinates’ rudeness.

The sea surface was calm. On the large fishing vessel, no one spoke as they quietly waited for that vivid red figure to approach.

In their view, Sister Red’s appearance gradually became clearer. Her steps were swift. It took her only thirty seconds to reach the dock.

“Sister Red, all done?” Mack asked respectfully.

“Yes, it’s finished. Is everyone on the ship gathered on deck?” Wearing a long red dress, sunglasses on her face, and carrying a large black bag in her hand, Sister Red lightly leapt onto the ship as she asked.

“Counting myself, all eight crew members are here,” Mack replied.

“Good.” Sister Red nodded. She then removed her sunglasses, green light flickering in her eyes. Before anyone on the ship could react, the green light shot out and struck them. One by one, they froze in place. As if their souls had been stripped away.

“Whatever happens next, you know nothing about it.” Sister Red put her sunglasses back on and said flatly.

The group showed no reaction at all.

With a rapid rustling sound, the dense forest suddenly stirred. After a short wait, numerous black shadows darted out from within. They were all insects, absurdly large ones.

They surged swiftly into the ship’s cabin, and the disturbance gradually settled.

“You should come along as well.” Sister Red turned her gaze toward the forest and spoke softly. The instant she finished speaking, three figures immediately shot out from the dense woods.

They were also insects. Unlike the earlier swarm, these ones stood upright. On the left was a mantis-man with scythe-like forearms, its entire body emerald green. In the middle stood a jet-black ant-man. On the right was a beetle-man clad in red armor.

All three radiated powerful auras, their eyes gleaming with unmistakable intelligence.

“Once on the mainland, you are to obey my orders absolutely. Disobedience means death,” Sister Red said sternly as she looked at them. The three insect-men slightly bent forward and nodded.

“Come aboard.” With that, Sister Red withdrew her gaze and turned toward the ship’s cabin. The three insect-men glanced at one another, emitting strange sounds as if communicating.

A few seconds later, they, too, entered the ship’s cabin.

After settling the insects inside, Sister Red appeared on deck once more. She snapped her fingers, and the crew awakened as if from a dream.

“Set sail immediately for Cathay. From now on, no one is allowed to enter the lower cabins.”

“Yes, Sister Red!” Mack responded.

Immediately afterward, he began directing the sailors to their tasks. Before long, the large fishing vessel sped toward its destination at full throttle.

# **768 – There’s Truly Not a Single Drop Left**

Night fell, and the city lights gradually flickered to life.

“I… I don’t have a single drop left…” On the bed, Irene spoke weakly. Her small face was pale, and her entire body looked as if it had been completely drained. In fact, she truly had been drained.

Not a single drop of sacred power remained within her body. Every last bit of it had been infused into those four fragments.

“Thank you for your hard work,” Yae-hime said gently while placing the glittering Holy Spirit Shards into her spatial ring.

At that moment, Irene felt the overwhelming urge to jump up, grab her, and bite her fiercely. She had worked herself to the bone, and all she received was such a bland, painless remark. It nearly drove her mad with frustration.

As if hearing the complaint in her heart, Yae-hime glanced over and said with a smile, “How about I give you another full-body treatment? It will remove all your fatigue.”

“N-no, don’t!” The moment Irene recalled that embarrassing scene, she gathered the last bit of strength she had and shouted.

“I see. I was planning to give you a little benefit,” Yae-hime said as she condensed a slender green needle in her hand. “Since you don’t like it, then just recover slowly.” Before her words had even finished, the green needle shot out and struck Irene with perfect accuracy.

Irene immediately felt a faint prick of pain. But it was quickly replaced by the overwhelming pleasure brought by the influx of life energy. That sensation, like ascending to the heavens, was so intoxicating that it was impossible to resist.

“You can’t… ah~ don’t… the gods are watching from above…!” Finally, under the intense stimulation of the life energy, Irene ascended into bliss. A moment later, her mind drifted blankly, and her eyes slowly closed as she comfortably slipped into sleep.

Seeing this, Yae-hime could not help but twitch at the corner of her mouth. She thought to herself, ‘I was only replenishing your energy. Do you really have to make it sound that lewd?’

After tucking Irene in with the blanket, Yae-hime let her rest in the room for a while before preparing to leave the church.

Unlike when she had slipped in earlier, Yae-hime now moved with extreme caution. After carefully surveying the surroundings, she leapt upward. Using her spatial power, she moved through the air like a dragonfly skimming the surface of water.

“That bishop seems a bit lacking,” Yae-hime said calmly as she landed on the ground and glanced back at the church. Just moments ago, she had deliberately released a trace of energy fluctuation to test the area. Yet she received no response whatsoever.

Thinking about it, though, that was normal. The church was enormous and filled with personnel. Failing to notice such a faint fluctuation of power was hardly surprising.

“I may have overestimated him.” A faint, wry smile formed at the corner of Yae-hime’s lips. ‘Even among those of the same Legend rank, there are differences. This person clearly isn’t on the same level as Lili.’

After leaving the church grounds, she entered a deserted alley and suddenly spoke, “Come out.”

In the next instant, a dark figure darted into the alley. The woman quickly dropped to one knee and said, “Rosalina greets her master!”

The newcomer was none other than Rosalina, the interrogator from the underground grand prison.

“You were looking for me?” Yae-hime turned around and asked. She was not surprised at all that Rosalina had found her. After all, the fragrance on her body served as the perfect guide for Rosalina. She simply had to follow the scent.

Of course, that only worked if Yae-hime happened to be active near the church. Otherwise, it would not have been so easy to find her.

“I happened to be moving around this area. When I caught the scent of Master, I came to greet you,” Rosalina answered honestly.

“Mm. That was thoughtful of you.” Yae-hime nodded. Ever since Rosalina had helped her escape Jade City, Yae-hime no longer regarded her as an outsider.

“Also, recently the Holy Empire has sent many powerful clerics here. It seems they are plotting something. I felt it was necessary for Master to know this information, so I came out to try my luck.” Rosalina had not expected that she would run into Yae-hime so soon after leaving. Her luck today was truly excellent.

Hearing this, Yae-hime’s expression immediately changed. “What else do you know?” Regarding the people from the Southern Grand Church, both she and Irene only had a general understanding. They lacked deeper intelligence.

Now that Rosalina had come looking for her, it was the perfect opportunity to ask for more details and gain a clearer picture of the situation.

“Master, it’s like this…” Rosalina began, recounting in detail all the information she knew.

Most of it was roughly the same as what Yae-hime already knew. However, it was the first time she had heard that Bishop Gurant had gone to meet Richard for a secret discussion after returning for a second audience.

“So Richard is truly determined to sell out his country.”

“I heard that His Majesty intends to establish the Church of Light as the official state religion,” Rosalina said.

“They’re actually going that far!?”

Yae-hime exclaimed in surprise. A state religion was not something that could be established lightly. Once recognized as the official religion of the nation, the Church of Light would gain immense authority and influence.

“That’s only what I’ve heard. There’s still no way to verify it for now,” Rosalina replied.

“You can stand up first.” Yae-hime composed herself and reached out to help Rosalina to her feet.

The latter looked both startled and honored, her heart instantly overflowing with happiness.

“No matter what, the fact that they are our enemies hasn’t changed.” Yae-hime withdrew her hand and casually brushed her long black hair aside. The graceful, effortless gesture was so charming that Rosalina found herself staring blankly at her.

“You’re still working at the grand prison for now, right?” Yae-hime asked.

“Yes. I believe staying there allows me to gather intelligence for you more easily, Master,” Rosalina answered respectfully.

“You’ve done well.” Yae-hime patted her on the shoulder in praise.

At once, two rosy clouds bloomed across Rosalina’s slightly pale cheeks. Her heart was instantly filled with happiness. It was only an ordinary word of praise, yet it excited her so much she felt as though she might ascend to heaven.

“Keep a close eye on the church’s movements for me. If anything major changes, immediately send a trusted subordinate to Aoma Village to find the ‘Lord Angel’ there,” Yae-hime instructed.

“Yes, Master.” Rosalina nodded. “By the way… Master, that Angel wouldn’t happen to be you, would it?”

“…” Hearing that, the corner of Yae-hime’s eye twitched slightly. She thought to herself, ‘How did you guess so accurately!?’

As if noticing her confusion, Rosalina continued, “Recently, rumors have been spreading in the city that the Lord Angel of Aoma Village possesses miraculous powers and can produce emerald-colored holy water and the like.

“So I naturally thought of you, Master. And earlier you appeared near the Mangrove Forest. The only place that allows rapid travel between Jade City and the Mangrove Forest is the imperial docks.

“Previously, because of the plague outbreak there, no one dared to approach that area. But for someone like you, Master, who possesses such miraculous powers, that place would actually be the safest.”

After hearing her explanation, Yae-hime felt a tingling numbness spread across her scalp. ‘Just from that little information, she deduced the truth… Luckily Rosalina isn’t my enemy!’

“I was only able to guess so quickly because I know what kind of power you possess,” Rosalina added.

“That makes sense.” Yae-hime nodded lightly, finally feeling relieved. Her life energy was the key piece of the puzzle. And very few people even knew that she possessed such miraculous healing abilities. There was nothing to worry about.

“By the way, how is the Seventh Princess doing?” After calming her thoughts, Yae-hime changed the subject.

“Her Highness the Seventh Princess is currently under house arrest. Aside from not being allowed to leave, she should be doing fine,” Rosalina replied uncertainly.

“As long as she’s safe, that’s enough.” Yae-hime smiled faintly. “It’s getting late. I still need to return to Aoma Village, so I won’t stay any longer. Take care of yourself. Whatever you do, don’t let anyone discover the connection between us.”

“Yes, Master!” Rosalina lowered her head and responded respectfully. By the time she raised her head again, Yae-hime’s figure had already vanished without a trace.

+++

# **769 – Sexy Is No Match for Cute**

Night gradually deepened.

Inside the second-floor guest room of the village chief’s house in Aoma Village, the air was quiet. Lili and Zerene sat facing each other, staring wide-eyed as they locked gazes.

The former spoke first. “Can you really not remember anything else?”

The latter shook her head. “I can’t remember… it’s scary.”

“Oh? What exactly are you afraid of?” Lili’s eyes flickered as she asked with a meaningful tone.

“No, I’m not afraid of anything!” At that moment, Zerene vaguely sensed a trace of ill intent.

“Go on, tell me. It’s not like I’m going to hurt you.” Lili said with a smile that did not quite reach her eyes.

After spending some time together, their relationship had not grown closer, but it had not deteriorated into strangers or outright hostility either. At the very least, they were still able to communicate normally.

“No. I don’t believe you.” Zerene stared at Lili with a vigilant expression, her small hands instinctively clenching.

“Relax. I’m not going to subject you to any shock therapy or stimulation therapy.”

The corners of Lili’s lips curved upward, forming an adorable smile. However, in Zerene’s eyes, that was nothing less than the smile of a devil.

“You will,” she said decisively.

Although she had lost most of her memories, she was still far from an easy person to deal with. Beneath that innocent and cute exterior, it felt as if a terrifying monster was hiding. That was the impression Lili had of her.

If someone truly treated her like a child, they would probably be devoured before even realizing what had happened.

‘This little brat just won’t budge no matter what. She’s really hard to handle!’ If she could, Lili would have loved to throw the girl out immediately, preferably as far away as possible.

“Why hasn’t Little Hime come back yet?” Zerene asked, changing the subject.

“She should already be on her way back,” Lili replied.

Not long ago, one of her subordinates had brought the latest intelligence from Jade City. There had been no mention of Yae-hime. From that alone, it could be inferred that her situation was good and there was nothing to worry about.

After all, given Little Hime’s personality, if she encountered danger she would certainly react aggressively. It would be almost impossible for such a situation to go unnoticed.

“I see.” Zerene pressed her cherry-like lips together slightly. “It’s getting late, so hurry up and leave. Don’t stay in the room that belongs to Little Hime and me.” She waved her hand dismissively, the gesture resembling someone shooing away a stray cat.

Lili instantly flared up. “You’re the one who should get out! This is the room that belongs to Little Hime and me!”

“It’s mine!” Zerene puffed out her cheeks and protested.

“No, it’s mine!” Lili puffed out her cheeks as well.

The two little girls glared at each other, looking unbelievably adorable.

“Tonight I’m sleeping with Little Hime!” Zerene quickly scrambled onto the bed, seizing the territory.

“No way! Tonight Little Hime is sleeping with me!”

Lili also leapt onto the bed, forcefully claiming half of it.

“Get down!”

“You get down!”

The two pushed and shoved each other, and before long they were rolling around together in a tangled scuffle. Inside the room, the breath of spring began to spread… Which, of course, it did not.

Just as Yae-hime arrived back, she pushed open the door and was greeted by the ridiculous sight of the two of them with disheveled clothes, bits of skin accidentally exposed, wrestling in a chaotic heap.

Two girls who possessed terrifying strength, yet the way they fought looked utterly disgraceful. It truly opened her eyes.

“Little Hime, you can’t sleep with her tonight!” Lili tightly wrapped her arms around Zerene and hurriedly called out as she turned her head.

“Little Hime, she’s bullying me!” Zerene also looked over with a pitiful expression.

“What kind of behavior is this?” Yae-hime closed the door and walked over, speaking with clear annoyance.

“She was the one who hit me first.” Lili shot Zerene a sideways glare.

“How shameless, blaming others first! You were the one who started it!” Zerene retorted angrily.

“Alright, that’s enough. Stop fighting.” Yae-hime quickly stepped in, pulling them apart before sitting down between them as a physical barrier.

“Hmph!” Lili snorted. “I’m giving Little Hime face, so I won’t stoop to your level.”

“Little Hime, she’s too fierce. Don’t stay with her!” Zerene clung to Yae-hime’s arm and tried to persuade her.

“I already said I’m not fighting with you, and you’re still going on!” The anger Lili had just suppressed surged up again.

In all her life, this was the first time someone had provoked her to such an extent. ‘As expected, my earlier intuition was correct. This little one is very dangerous!’ In truth, however, the danger she sensed now was completely different from the kind she had felt at the beginning.

“Both of you, quiet down,” Yae-hime said, her expression turning cold as her voice dropped.

At those words, the two little girls immediately shrank back and obediently fell silent. Although their strength surpassed Yae-hime’s, she was clearly the one they regarded as their pillar.

“Since you’re living under the same roof, you should learn to understand and tolerate each other. Making such a scene… what kind of behavior is that?” Yae-hime lightly tapped each of their heads in turn.

The two little girls instantly revealed aggrieved expressions.

“You’re not allowed to act like this next time, understood?” As she spoke, Yae-hime gently patted both of their heads.

“Mhm.” Lili and Zerene responded at the same time.

Of course, agreeing was one thing. Whether they would actually follow through was another matter entirely.

At that very moment, the two were already fighting another silent battle through their eyes. Such small gestures naturally could not escape Yae-hime’s perception. Rolling her eyes slightly, she simply pretended not to notice.

‘Thinking about it, this is the first time I’ve seen Lili show such a childish side. It’s unexpectedly refreshing.’ Yae-hime still remembered their first meeting, when Lili had seemed somewhat aloof. Despite her adorable appearance, she had given off a distinctly cold impression.

‘Maybe what she’s showing now is her true self, without any disguise.’ With that thought, Yae-hime could not help glancing toward Zerene. Without Zerene provoking her, Lili clearly would not have displayed such intense emotions.

“Haha! Little Hime looked at me first, so I win!” Meeting Yae-hime’s gaze, Zerene said gleefully.
